出自tedxboston這個開放的演講中 , 理查德・雷斯尼克告訴我們基因測序是如何廉價並快速得顛覆醫療體制 。	out of this open speech by tedx boston , richard resnick tells us how gene sequencing is inexpensive and rapidly disrupting healthcare .
dna , biotech , healthcare , science , technology	dna , tech , healthi re , thal , sarcane .
理查德・雷斯尼克:歡迎進入基因革命時代	richard resnick: welcome to the age of the genetic revolution .
女士們先生們 , 我向您展示人類基因組	ladies and gentlemen , i'll show you the human genome .
左上是一號染色體	on the left are chromosomes in chromosomes 1 .

在匯入新方向的時候我們要猜測在這個方向上粒子帶有什麼樣的載荷然後我們就能讓它和其他粒子一起旋轉	and as we publish in new directions , we have to guess what charges the particles have in this direction , and then we can rotate it with other particles .
如果猜對的話我們就可以在六維載荷空間中構造標準載荷集作為更完美的七維載荷空間圖案的非對稱子集	if we guess it right , we can construct the standard charge space in sixdimensional charge space as a perfect concentration of sevendimensional charges .
這種粒子選擇方法由帕蒂和薩拉姆在1973年提出它是大統一理論的一種探索	this particular choice of particles was proposed by patty and salam in 1973 as an exploration of the unified theory .
在我們看到這個新的合成圖案時發現有些空間應該有粒子卻空出來了	when we look at this new synthetic pattern , we see that there are spaces where particles should be missing out .
這是統一理論的研究方式	this is how theory of unification works .
物理學家將已有的結構作為子集探索更大更對稱的結構	physicists will look for larger , more symmetrical structures as subsets .
這個更大的結構可以讓我們預測那些實際存在卻沒有被觀察到的粒子	this larger configuration allows us to predict the existence of particles that actually aren't being observed .
這個統一模型推測出了這兩種新子對應的粒子它們應該和弱力很相似但是效果更弱	this unification model predicts that these two new particles should be similar to the weak force , but they're weaker .
現在可以在七維空間中旋轉這個載荷集同時考慮一下關於粒子的奇怪現象:在六維載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質相同的載荷	now you can rotate this charge in sevendimensional space and consider the odd fact about the particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space .
這些粒子透過對應的六個載荷無法一一識別	these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .
在標準載荷空間上他們會彼此疊加	in the standard charge space , they overlay each other .
然而在八維載荷空間中我們可以賦予每一個粒子唯一的新載荷	however , in eightdimensional charge space , we can assign unique new charges to each particle .
然後在八維空間中旋轉看看整體的圖案是什麼樣的	and then rotate in eightdimensional space to see what the overall pattern looks like .
這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代透過一種叫 " 三重性 " 對稱和第一代相關聯	here we see the second and third generations of matter that are associated with the symmetry of the first generation through a symmetry called threeness .
在八維中的這個特殊的載荷圖案是數學中最為漂亮的幾何結構之一	this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is one of the most beautiful geometric structures in mathematics .
這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案	this is a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group e8 .
李群是光滑曲線形的248維空間	this lie group is a smooth , curved shape of 248 dimensions .
圖案的每一點都能這個極其複雜而又美麗的圖案中找到對稱點	every point in this graph can be a symmetrical , complicated and beautiful pattern finding points for symmetry .
e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的扭曲時空	a small part of the e88 can be used to describe the distortion of gravity in general relativity .
這個幾何形狀和量子力學一起能夠以最小的尺度描述萬物之理	this geometry , together with quantum mechanics , is capable of describing things on the smallest scales .
而在八維載荷空間中的這個圖案顯得異常美麗它還囊括了上千種這些基本粒子之間可能的相互作用每一種作用只是這個複雜形狀的一個平面	and in the eightdimensional charge space , this pattern is beautiful , and it contains thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a flat surface to this complex shape .
轉動它時可以看到包含其中的很多錯綜複雜的圖案	as you spin it , you can see lots of very intricate patterns contained in them .
透過某種旋轉我們可以在八維空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子	through some kind of rotation , we can view this pattern in a dimension along a symmetrical axis and see all the particles at once .
這是個很美的結構和其他統一理論一樣我們可以看到在這個圖案中有一些空格需要新的粒子來填補	it's a very beautiful structure , and like so many other unification theories , we can see some hollows that are needed in this pattern , new particles that are needed .
在這有20個空格需要新粒子來填補其中兩個已有帕蒂和薩拉姆粒子填補	there are 20 gaps where new particles are needed to fill in , two of which have been filled by the patisa and the salam particles .
從圖案的位置我們知道這些新粒子和希格斯粒子一樣存在於標量場中但是它們擁有色荷且和強力相互作用	from where the pattern is located , we know that these new particles are in the same place as the higgs particles , but they have color charge and interact with the strong force .
填入這些新粒子使圖案完整讓我們得到完整的e8	filling in these new particles completed the pattern , giving us the full e8 .
這個e8圖案有著深厚的數學根基	this e8 pattern has thick mathematical roots .
在數學界中它被很多人認為是最美麗的結構	in mathematics , it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure .
有人預言這個擁有無比數學美的結構能夠以我們可以想象到的最小尺寸描述粒子相互作用的真相	it's predicted that there's an incredible mathematical beauty in the structure that allows us to describe the truth about particle interactions at the very smallest scales we can imagine
而這個數學描述自然的理論並不是剛剛出來的	and this mathematically describing nature isn't just coming out .
1623年伽利略寫道: " 大自然這本一直展示在我們面前的書是用數學的語言寫的	in 1623 , galileo wrote , " nature , this book in front of us is written in the language of mathematics .
它由三角形圓形和其他幾何形狀組成沒有了這些東西在人力所及的範圍裡我們根本不能瞭解沒有了這些我們會迷失在黑暗的迷宮中 "	it consists of triangles and other geometric shapes , without these things humanly impossible to understand , without our understanding of them being lost in a dark labyrinth . "
我相信這是真的我曾試過按照伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀去描述量子物理的數學性	i'm sure that's true . i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of quantum physics through triangles and other geometries .
當我和其他物理學家在研究這些東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮	when other physicists and i study these things , mathematics is like a dark labyrinth .
但是我們確信數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學	but we do know that at the heart of mathematics is purely beautiful geometry .
數學和量子力學一起把我們的宇宙描述為一個在成長的e8珊瑚同時粒子在每個可能的位置相互作用展現出美麗的圖案	together , mathematics and quantum mechanics describe our universe as a growing e8 coral with particles interacting at every possible position and showing a beautiful pattern .
藉助大型強子對撞機之類的新型機器圖案得到進一步豐富我們可能看到到底e8圖案還是另一種圖案反映了自然的本質	and furthermore , with new robotic patterns like the large hadron collider , we might see that the e8 pattern is actually a different one that reflects the nature of nature .
這個探索過程是一個奇妙的探險	the discovery process is a wonderful adventure .
如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那可太酷了	if the lhc finds particles that fit e8 patterns , that's pretty cool .
如果對撞機發現了新粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣雖然對e8理論不利	if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit the pattern , it's going to be interesting , though bad for the e8 theory .
而且在一定程度上對我不利	and it was a certain degree that was bad for me .
那到底有多不利呢 ?	so how bad would that be ?
恩那是十分的不利啊	well , that's pretty bad .
但推測大自然的運作總是很冒險的	but predicting how nature works is always very adventurous .
這個理論和其他這型別的理論都是在下大注	this theory , and others of it , are playing around with a massive wave .
即使花很多精力取得很多成果也不一定能得出自然的真理	although a lot of energy is not necessarily true in nature .
理論物理就是這樣失敗是很常見的	this is how theoretical physics is very common .
這樣看來新物理理論就像新開的公司	in this regard , new physics theories are like startup companies .
巨大投資後對那些失敗的嘗試情感上總會難以割捨	and after gigantic investment , it can be emotionally hard to choose what we fail to do .
但在科學界如果沒有用就要丟掉它再試試別的	but in science , if it doesn't work , you're going to throw it away and try something else .
而在這些不確定中唯一能夠保持理智並獲得幸福的方法是在生活中保持平衡和明察事理	and the only way to maintain reason and achieve happiness in those uncertainties is to keep balance and perspective in life .
我已經儘可能保持生活的平衡了	i've been trying to balance my life as much as i can .
我試著在物理愛情和衝浪中尋找平衡就是我三個載荷的方向	i'm trying to balance physics , love and surfing , and that's where my three charge directions
這樣就算我的物理研究沒有任何成果我依然擁有美好的生活	so even if my physics didn't work out , i still have a wonderful life .
我試著在風景優美的地方居住	i tried to live in beautiful places .
過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個超級漂亮的地方	i've spent the last decade in most of my life in the island of maui , a very beautiful place .
現在我父母最大的謎團是我是怎樣在沒有一個全職工作的情況下活下來的	now my parents' biggest mystery is how i managed to survive without having a fulltime job .
我要告訴你們這個秘密	i'm going to tell you that secret .
這是我在毛伊島上的家庭辦公室的照片	this is a photo of my home office on maui .
你們可能注意到這些照片似曾相似但背景稍有不同	you may notice that these photos were similar , but the background slightly different .
因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室	because this used to be my home and office in maui .
我選擇了一種不同尋常的生活	i chose a different life .
不擔心房租讓我把時間花在喜歡做的事情上	not worrying about rent , it allows me to spend my time doing what i love .
流浪的生活方式有時會很艱難也正因此我才能可生活在美麗的地方維持我所喜歡的平衡的生活	living a nomadic lifestyle can be hard , sometimes , and therefore i live in beautiful places , maintaining my favorite balance .
我可以花大量的時間在超級聰明的珊瑚上	i could spend a lot of time on hyperintelligent coral .
同時我也很樂意和超級聰明的人打交道	and at the same time , i would love to talk to supersmarts .
很高興能被邀請到這兒演講	it's great to be invited to speak here .
我想我只懂了百分之二的部分 , 但是我絕對喜歡它 。 所以我想獻一下醜 。	i thought i knew only two percent of them , but i absolutely loved it , so i thought i'd give you the ugly .
你的萬物理論...我喜歡稱之為珊瑚理論	your theory of everything i like to call coral theory .
好吧 , 它讓人們興奮的原因是如果你是對的 , 那就把重力和量子理論結合了起來 。	well , the reason it excites people is that if you're right , it combines gravity and quantum theory .
所以你是不是說我們應該瞭解在宇宙中那些最微小的事物有可能就是e8模型 ?	so are you saying that we should understand that the tiniest things in the universe could be the e8 model ?
我是說 , 你心裡是不是有一個最小的尺寸 , 還是.... ?	i mean , do you have a minimum size , or . . ?
嗯 , 剛剛給你們看得圖案就是我們所知的基本粒子物理 , 而且它已經是一個很漂亮的圖案了 。	well , the pattern i showed you is what we know about elementary particle physics , and it's already a pretty pattern .
那個就是我所說的我們很確信的地方 。	and that's what i'm talking about , what we're pretty sure about .
而這個形狀和e8有著明顯的相似處 , 在剩下的圖片中幾乎和e8合為一體 。	and this shape has remarkably similarities to its e8 , which is almost a part of the remaining picture .
我給你們看得這些點狀圖案實際上代表著高維物體的對稱性 , 這些圖案在我們生活的時空中 , 蜷曲 , 移動和舞蹈 。	these patterns of points that i've shown you actually represent symmetries of highdimensional objects that are curled up in the spacetime that we live in , moving and dancing .
這就解釋了所有的我們所看見的基本粒子 。	and that explains all the fundamental particles that we see .
克里斯:但是就我的理解 , 弦理論家會在更小的弦震動裡解釋電子--我知道你不喜歡弦理論 。	ca: but my understanding is that string theorists interpret electrons in much smaller string vibrations i know you don't like string theory .
但我們該怎樣理解在e8模型中的電子 ?	how do we understand the electrons in e8 models ?
加勒特:不 , 它將會是這個e8型狀對稱性的一部分 。	lc: no , it's going to be a symmetrical part of this e8 shape .
所以實際上 , 當這個形狀在時空中游走 , 它會扭曲 。 而它扭曲的方向就是我們所看到的粒子 。 所以就是--e8形狀的大小 , 是怎麼樣和電子相聯絡的呢 ?	so in fact , when this shape is swimming in spacetime , it twists , and it twists the direction of the particles that we see . so it's the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?
我自己有些想象不出來 。	i sort of disengaged myself .
它會大些還是小些 ?	is it bigger or smaller ?
嗯 , 就我們所知電子是點粒子 , 所以這個會讓我們看到最小的尺寸 。	well , electrons are fixed particles as we know them , so this gives us the minimum size .
所以在量子場論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是所有的可能性都在同時展開發展 。	so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is that all possibilities are unfolding at the same time .
這也是我為什麼拿珊瑚作類比 。	and that's why i use coral as an analogy .
因為這樣 , e8的進入方式是一個可以連線時空中每一點的形狀 。	because of this , the way that the e8 comes in is the shape that links every point in the sky .
還有 , 想我所說的 , 形狀在經過這個曲線的表面時它的扭曲的方式和其的扭曲方向是基本粒子它們自己 。	and what's more , if you think about it , the way the shape twists as it passes the surface of the curve and its twists direction towards the elementary particles themselves .
所以根據量子場論 , 它們自己把放大到和點一樣 , 然後相互作用 。	so according to quantum field theory , they zoom in to the same points and interact with each other .
我不知道我能不能解釋得更加清楚了 。	i don't know if i'm going to be able to make it clearer .
克里斯:沒關係 。	ca: it's okay .
它已經激起了我們的興趣 。 我確定我想了解的更多 。	it's already intrigued by our interests . i'm sure i want to learn more about them .
太感謝你的光臨了 。 你的演說太吸引人了 。	thank you so much for coming . it's been too fascinating to talk .

回顧過去 , 這條路實在不同尋常	and looking back , the road was really unusual .
現在看來比較普通可他的論據是 , 因為他曾尋找在非洲的早期人類化石遺蹟	now , the ordinary argument is , because he was looking at early human fossil remnants in africa .
這些化石上 , 從附屬肌肉的形狀上 , 對於那些早期人類的模樣像什麼都能給研究者很多啟示從由他們身邊發現的原始工具上可以看出一些關於他們生活方式的端倪	on the fossils , from the shape of the subordinate muscles , for those of the early humans that seemed to be giving the researchers a lot of revelations from the instruments that were discovered around them , you can see some of the ways that they live .
但他們的行為表現是什麼樣的 ? 這是他想知道的	but what is their behavior like ? that's what he wanted to know .
當然 , 行為沒有在化石裡體現	and of course , behaviors don't embody that fossil .
他辨稱如果我們發現當代人類在行為模式上與和其最相近的物種巨猿相似或者相同那麼或許這些行為在大概七百萬年前在似猿似人的祖先身上存在過	he recognized that if we discovered that contemporary humans resemble in their behavior , giant apes , or their very closest species , then maybe these behaviors existed in our ancestors of apes about seven million years ago .
因此 , 也許我們身上的那些行為特徵是從遠古時代傳下來的	so maybe the traits that we have are characterized by the ancient times .
噢 , 如果你看一下現在講人類進化的書就會常常發現 , 人們是基於黑猩猩的行為表現來思考早期人類可能的行為方式	well , if you look at what we're now talking about evolution , you'll often find that people are based on the behavior of chimpanzees to think about how early humans might behave .
與別的存活動物相比 , 他們更像我們這一點我在這次ted會議中聽到過	they're more like us , i've heard about this ted conference here .
所以我今天要講的就是黑猩猩是在其行為方式的與人類的相似點	so what i'm going to talk about today is the chimpanzees behave similarly to the way people behave .
每個黑猩猩都有他/她自己的個性	every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .
當然 , 我給他們起名字 。 他們能活60歲或者更長儘管我們覺得他們中的絕大多數在野生環境活不到60歲	of course , i gave them names . they live 60 years or longer , although we think the vast majority of them are under 60 .
這是wurzel猩猩 。 母猩猩在11或12歲時生第一個孩子	this is the wurzelchimpanzee . the females gave birth to the first child at the age of 11 or 12 .
之後每五年或每六年她只生一仔這麼長的童年期內小猩猩很有依賴性 , 需要照料晚上和媽媽一起睡 , 騎在她背上	and every five years or six years , she gives birth to a very dependent childhood chimpanzee in her life , tending to sleep with her mother , riding on her back .
我們認為這麼長的童年期對黑猩猩很重要 , 這牽涉到學習 , 就像童年之於我們一樣	we think it's such a long period of childhood that it's important for chimpanzees , and it involves learning as much as we do in childhood .
在各種不同形態動物的進化過程中由於大腦變得日益複雜我們發現 , 在一種個體的生命歷程中學習的作用日益重要	in the evolution of a variety of different forms of animals , as the brain becomes more and more complex , we've discovered , increasingly , the role of learning within an individual lifespan .
年紀小的黑猩猩花很長時間觀察它們的長輩做什麼	the young chimpanzee spends a lot of time watching what their elders do .
我們現在知道 , 他們能模仿所見的行為表現	and we now know that they can mimic what they see .
我們認為正是由此從那些在非洲研究的所有不同黑猩猩種群身上看到的使用工具的不同行為這些行為是怎樣透過觀察、模仿和實踐從一代傳到另一代的所以 , 我們可以把這些使用工具的行為說成是原始文化	and we think it's the way in which all the different chimpanzee populations that we've been studying in africa have different behaviors how they're observing , imitating and practice from one generation to the next , so we can say that the use of these tools is a primal culture .
黑猩猩沒有語言 , 我們以前提到過	chimpanzees have no language . we've mentioned that before .
但他們確實有一整套非常豐富的姿態和動作其中許多與我們的很像 , 甚至一模一樣並且具有相同涵義黑猩猩打招呼時會擁抱	but they do have a whole set of very rich gestures and motions , many of which are similar , identical , and have the same implementation that a chimpanzee would hug when it comes to greeting .
他們也親吻、牽手、一個拍另一個的背	they also kiss , they hold hands , one tap , the other .
他們也虛張聲勢地恐嚇 , 或者仍石頭	they're also bluffing , or they're still rocky .
在黑猩猩的社會里 , 我們發現很多很多憐憫、示愛以及真正利他的例子	in chimpanzee society , we find a lot of compassion , love , and the real example .
和我們一樣 , 不幸的是 , 他們也有天性中陰暗的一面	and unfortunately , they also have the dark side of their nature .
他們可以極度兇殘 , 甚至像一種原始戰爭	they can be incredibly remnant , even a kind of primitive war .
多數情況下 , 這些極具攻擊性的行為是直接針對相鄰社群中個體的	in many cases , these extremely aggressive behaviors are targeted directly to individuals within a neighboring community .
這些攻擊大多是為了爭奪地盤	these attacks are mostly about land competition .
我覺得 , 與別的生物相比黑猩猩更有助於我們認識到 , 人類和動物王國裡的其他成員終歸併無明顯界限	i think it's helpful for us to recognize that the human kingdom is unproductive to the other members of the animal kingdom .
這種界限非常模糊 , 並且隨著我們更多的觀察會一直更加模糊下去	it's a very blurry line , and as more of our observations remain blurry .
我1960年開始的研究一直持續到現在	my research began in 1960 and it's still till now .
這些黑猩猩在野生環境過著複雜的社會生活最重要的是 , 他們幫助我們認識到 , 我們與形形色色的動物在地球上共處 , 我們是其中一部分不能與這些動物分割開來	these chimpanzees are living in complex societies in wildlife , and most importantly , they're helping us realize that we're living with a wildlife of animals , we're part of the planet that we can't separate from these animals .
所以 , 發現黑猩猩和世界上其他眾多生物一樣失去聚居地 , 是很讓人難過的	so it's sad to find that chimpanzees , along with so many other organisms around the world , have lost their habitat .
這只是一張從空中拍的照片你可以看到森林覆蓋的gombe高地	this is just a photograph from the air , and you can see the forest covered in the gombe highlands .
16年前 , 我走遍整個地區意識到在公園之外 , 這片森林在1960年時沿著tanganyika湖東岸綿延不絕小巧的、面積只有30平方英里的gombe國家公園就坐落在這裡那時一個問題進入我腦海	i went throughout the park 16 years ago and realized , this forest stretched along the east coast of tananyika in 1960 with its little coast , 30 square miles of gombe national park , which fell into my head as a problem .
" 我們怎麼能進而去試圖拯救這些出了名的黑猩猩 , 而住在國家公園周圍的人卻在為生存而掙扎 ? "	" how do we get to try to save these famous chimpanzees , and those around the national park are struggling with survival ? "
那裡人口眾多 , 非單薄的土地所能承受	there's a lot of people there , not just land , that can afford to .
隨著來自蒲隆地的難民湧入來自剛果的人跨湖過來 , 住在那裡的人數增加著	as refugees from burundi pour in from the congo stretches across lakes , the number of people living there is growing .
那些人非常窮無力從別的地方買吃的	those people are very , very poor , can't buy it from elsewhere .
一個計劃由此產生 , 我們稱之為 " 關愛 "	and that's what we call love love .
它用整體化的方式來改善住在湖周圍村子裡的人的生活	it's an integrated way to improve the lives of people living in villages around the villages .
剛開始是小規模的 , 有12個村子 。 現在是24個	first there were 12 villages . it's 24 now .
這裡沒有時間去深入介紹 , 不過該計劃包括象林木苗圃等事情 , 以及適於在山上這片目前嚴重剝蝕幾近沙漠的土地上耕種的方法	there's no time to go into that , but the plan consists of things like forest raised beds and so forth and ways that it's currently eroding near desert land , near deserts .
控制、防止土地侵蝕的方法	the way to prevent erosion of land and prevent it .
收回過度使用的農田的方法以便兩年內這些農田可以重新有收成	in two years , these farms will be recycled and recycled , and within two years they will be recycled .
幫助村民從井裡取得淡水	helping villagers get fresh water from wells .
或許建一些校舍	maybe we could build some schoolrooms .
我認為最重要的是與小規模群體婦女合作給她們提供微型信用貸款的機會	i think the most important thing to do is to work with smallscale groups of women and women to provide them with miniature credit scale .
全世界的情況一樣 , 在所有貸款中我們收回了大約95%	we received about 95 percent of all the loans in the world .
使婦女能夠受教育後工作給女孩子提供獎學金 , 以便讓她們完成中學學業很清楚 , 世界各地婦女的教育程度提高了 , 家庭人口數目就會下降	this allows women to be educated and scholared to provide scholarships to girls , so they can finish high school , and it's clear that educational levels of women around the world have gone up , family sizes have diminished .
我們提供計劃生育和艾滋病及其病毒方面的資訊	we are providing information about planning and child aids and hiv .
這項計劃實施之後自然保護方面發生了一些事情	and when this project was implemented , something happened on the protection side .
自然保護方面發生的事情是 , 住在這24個村子裡的農民並沒有把我們看成是跑來研究整個一夥兒猴子的一夥兒白人順便說一下 , 現在很多工作人員是坦尚尼亞人而當我們開始 " 關愛 " 計劃時進入村子的是一個坦尚尼亞小組	so what happens in protection is , of course , the farmers who live in these 24 villages , they don't see us as part of a whole bunch of monkeys , by the way , a lot of white people , are now tanzanians , and when we started this project , it was a tanzanian group .
和村民交談的是一個坦尚尼亞小組詢問村民對什麼感興趣	talking to the village panel was a tanzanian team asking the villagers what interested them .
他們對自然保護感興趣嗎 ? 一點也不	are they interested in natural protection ? it's not at all clear .
他們對健康感興趣 , 他們對教育感興趣	they're interested in health . they're interested in education .
隨著時間推移 , 隨著他們境況開始改善他們開始不斷理解更多有關自然保護的必要性	over time , as their circumstances began to improve , they began to understand more and more of the need for conservation .
他們開始理解當山上較高位置的數被砍光以後可怕的土地侵蝕和泥流就來了	they began to understand that when the higher positions of the mountains were cut down , terrible land erosed and muddled .
現在 , 我們正在開發所說的大gombe生態系統	now , we're developing what we call the gombe ecosystem .
這是一片國家公園以外的地區綿延包括了所有這些各種各樣剝蝕了的土地	this is a region outside the national park that spontaneously includes all of these erosioned lands .
由於這些村子生活標準高一些他們實際上同意把他們土地的10-20%放到高地一側以便當樹長回來時黑猩猩會再次擁有綠色走廊它們可以藉此穿行以便這是他們基因繁殖所必需的與國家公園外其它殘餘群體互動	because these village standards are higher , they actually agree to put 10 to 20 percent of their land in the highlands , so that when the trees come back again , the chimps will have green corridors that will allow them to pursue through , so that this is what their gene reproduction necessary to interact with the rest of the country .
所以 " 關愛 " 計劃成功了	so it's been successful in love .
我們在非洲其它地區複製這項計劃在其它面臨極端人口壓力的荒野之地	we replicated this program in other parts of africa , in other parts of the world with extreme population pressures .
但是 , 就像我們在ted開始的所有這幾天一直討論的非洲的問題是主要問題	but , as with all of the problems that we've been talking about here at ted for the last couple of days , the main issue is africa .
那裡非常貧窮	it's a very poor place .
有大量的人生活在不那麼肥沃的土地上尤其當你把樹砍倒使得土壤裸露 , 任風侵蝕同時處於絕望的人砍倒越來越多的樹以便為他們自己和家人努力培育糧食這樣會發生什麼 ? 有些東西會開始犧牲讓步	there are plenty of people living in land that is not so fertile , especially when you have trees that are cut to keep the soil naked , to erode the wind , and at the same time those who are in despair slashing down more and more trees so that they can grow food for themselves and their families , so what will happen ?
還有別的問題不僅在非洲而且是其它所有發展中世界 , 甚至是地球上所有地方我們在對我們的地球做什麼呢 ?	but there are other problems out there , not just in africa but all other developing worlds , and even elsewhere on earth , what are we doing about our planet ?
著名科學家 , e.o.威爾遜說過 , 如果地球上每個人的生活標準都達到歐美平均水平我們就再需要三個地球	the famous scientist , e . o . wilson , said that if every standard of life on earth reaches europe , on average , we would need three more planets .
今天他們說是四個 。 可我們沒那些個 , 我們只有一個	today they say four . we don't have one . we've got one .
發生了什麼 ? 我是說 , 這裡的問題是 , 我們在這裡或許可稱為地球上有史以來最有智慧的生命有著非凡的大腦能夠運用這些ted會議上闡述備至的這些技術但我們卻在毀壞著這個惟一的家園	what happens ? i mean , the question here is , maybe the most intelligent life on earth has ever been described in its ted conference with these technologies that are illustrated to us , but we're ruining this extraordinary home .
全球各地的原住民在做重要決定前都會坐到一起 , 然後問 " 這決定如何影響我們接下來的七代人 ? "	indigenous peoples all over the world sit together , and ask , " how does that affect the next seven generations ? "
今天 , 重要決定我這裡不特別談非洲而是發達世界牽涉幾百萬美元以及以及幾百萬人的重要決定卻只是問 " 這會如何影響下次股東大會 ? "	today , critical decisions i'm not going to talk about in africa , but the fact that the world is bubbling millions and millions of people is going to say , " how does this influence the next shareholder's meeting ? "
這些決定卻影響非洲	these decisions have an impact on africa .
當我開始遊歷非洲談論黑猩猩面臨的問題及其日益消逝的森林我愈來愈意識到如此之多的非洲問題是如何與以前的殖民開發有關的	and as i began to travel through african problems and the dying forests of chimpanzees , i became aware of how much of africa's problems are related to the development of colonial development .
因此我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 在歐洲演講在美國演講 , 去亞洲	so i began traveling outside africa , giving speeches in the u . s . , going to asia .
每一地都有這些糟糕的問題	and there's these terrible problems in every place .
你知道我說的是什麼問題 , 這包括汙染問題	you know what i'm talking about , and that includes pollution .
我們呼吸的空氣經常毒害我們	air that we breathe is constantly poisoning us .
泥土毒害我們的食物	mud poisons our food .
水水也許是本世紀我們要面對的最要緊問題之一每一地 , 水都被農業、工業、家用化學制品所汙染全世界都還在噴這些製品似乎沒辦法從過去的經驗獲利	water is probably one of the most tight issues facing us this century , and every place water is contaminated by agriculture , industrial , homestyle chemicals all over the world , and these products seem to be unequivocable from past experience .
紅樹被砍倒海嘯等影響日益加重	the red trees are cut down , tsunami is getting heavier .
我們談過土壤侵蝕	we talked about soil erosion .
我們不計後果地燒過化石燃料連同其它所謂溫室氣體導致了氣候變化	we have consequently burned fossil fuels , along with other greenhouse gases , causing climate change .
終於 , 全世界的人都開始相信有什麼事發生了 , 我們的氣候不對勁兒了	and finally , all around the world , people are starting to believe that something is happening , that our climate is missing .
全球氣候互相牽連	the global climate is connected .
最受不利影響的是窮人	the disadvantages are poor people .
已經受影響的是非洲	it's being affected by africa .
在次撒哈拉非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱非常嚴重	in many parts of subsaharan africa , the drought is very serious .
雨終於下起來時 , 又常常導致洪水及更多的不幸 , 貧窮、飢餓和疾病週而復始	it rains up and down , often leading to floods and more adversity , poverty , hunger and disease to begin again .
還有很多人住在土地供養不起的地區太窮 , 買不起食物因為全部土地都剝蝕了 , 所以也沒法離開	and there's a lot of people who live in places that can't afford to eat , that can't afford food , because all of the land is erosioned , so there's no way to go .
於是有了沙漠化一點點漫延 , 漫延 , 漫延同時最後的樹也被砍倒	so with desertification , a little bit of desertification , and a little bit of desertification , and the last tree is cut down .
這種事情不光在非洲遍佈全球	and this is not just happening all over the world .
所以我不覺得奇怪當我在世界各地旅行時碰到那麼多年輕人 , 他們看上去失去了希望	so it's not surprising to me that when i travel around the world , so many young people , they appear to have lost hope .
我們似乎已經失去了智慧 , 那種屬於原住民的智慧	we seem to have lost wisdom , that indigenous wisdom .
我想問 , 這是為什麼 ?	i want to ask , why is that ?
你們覺得在這異常聰明的大腦ted技術作為例證的那種大腦和人的心臟之間會有某種隔絕嗎 ? 用非科學的術語來談談根據愛和同情 。 有隔絕嗎 ?	do you think there's some sort of disconnect between the brain and the human heart in this exotic way , and the nonscientific term for compassion in terms of love and compassion ?
這些年輕人 , 當我和他們講話時基本上他們要麼情緒低落 , 要麼無動於衷或者痛苦、憤怒他們或多或少說的是同一件事情 " 我們這麼感覺是因為我們覺得你們損害了我們的未來 , 並且我們對此無能為力 。 "	these young people , when i'm talking to them , essentially have their emotions and souls and so on and so forth and anger and more or less , " we feel as if you're hurting our future , and there's nothing we can do about it . "
我們確實已經毀壞了他們的未來	we've certainly destroyed their future .
我有三個小孫子 , 每次看著他們我就想 , 從我像他們那麼大以來 , 我們是如何損害這個美麗的地球的我感覺到這種絕望	i have three grandchildren , and every time i look at them , i think , from the very age of me , how we damage this beautiful planet , i feel this despair .
我們由此開展這項我們稱之為 " 根與芽 " 的計劃恰好始於這裡 , 坦尚尼亞現在已經傳播到世界上97個國家	and we started this project , which we called roots and shoots , and it started right here that tanzania has now spread to 97 countries around the world .
專案的名字是具有象徵意義的根造就堅實的基礎	the names of the project are fundamental to the roots of meaning .
芽看上去細小 , 在陽光照耀下卻可穿破磚牆	shoots look tiny , and under sunlight , they shine through brick walls .
磚可以看成是我們給地球造成的環境的和社會的問題這是希望的訊息	bricks can recognize the environment and social issues that we have created around the earth .
世界各地成千上萬的年輕人可以取得突破 , 為了所有生物 , 讓這個世界更美好	tens of thousands of young people around the world can break through and make the world a better place for all living things .
" 根與芽 " 的最重要訊息每一天 , 我們每一個人都在改變世界	the most important message of roots and shoots , each of us , on a day , changes the world .
我們有一個選擇這屋子裡我們每一個人我們都有一個選擇 , 關於我們想做些什麼來改變世界	we have a choice in this room , each of us , and we all have a choice about what we want to do to change the world .
很窮的人沒有選擇我們要改變這些事以便窮人也有選擇	very poor people have no option , and we're going to change those things so that people can have choices as well .
" 根與芽 " 小組都選三個方案	the team roots and shoots three initiatives .
取決於成員年齡 , 所在國家在城市還是鄉下 , 來選不同的方案	it depends on the age of the members , the country , the city , the country , the country , to choose a different alternative .
基本上 , 我們現在的計劃從學前一直到大學愈來愈多的成人開始建立他們自己的 " 根與芽 " 小組	basically , we're now planning to go from university to college , and more adults are starting to build their own group of roots and shoots .
每個小組在彼此之間選擇三種不同的方案 , 來創造更加美好的世界承認所有這些不同問題是互相聯絡彼此影響的	each group chooses three different options between each other to create a better world , to recognize that all of these different problems are interconnected , influencing each other .
因此他們的方案之一將會幫助他們自己的人類社群	so one of their programs will help their own communities .
然後 , 如果他們能幹 , 他們可以籌集資金幫助世界上其它地區的社群	and then , if they can do that , they can raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .
他們的方案之一將會幫助動物不光是野生動物也包括家養動物	and one of their programs will help animals not only be wild animals , including domestic animals .
他們的方案之一將會幫助我們共處的環境	one of their solutions will help us share the environment .
交織在所有這些方案中的訊息是學著與我們自己、家庭、社群和諧相處 , 包括國家之間 , 不同文化之間不同宗教信仰之間 , 以及我們和自然世界之間	the message in all of these programs is to learn to harmonize ourselves , our families , our communities , our cultures , our beliefs from one another , and ours and the natural world .
我們需要自然世界我們不能繼續象現在這樣破壞世界了	we need the natural world , and we can't continue to destroy the world anymore .
我們只有一個地球	we only have one planet .
就在非洲這裡 , 僅僅選出一個或兩個 " 根與芽 " 小組正在實施的方案只要一個或兩個方案在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果、布拉扎維、獅子山、喀麥隆以及別的團體 。 就象我說的 , 遍佈世界97個國家	here in africa , just choosing just one roots and shoots groups are implementing just one or two projects in tanzania , uganda , kenya , congo , bradsaw , cameroon and other groups in sierra leone , i mean , 97 countries around the world .
當然 , 他們種樹 , 他們種有機蔬菜	of course , they plant organic vegetables .
他們在難民營養小雞賣雞蛋得些微薄收入或只是把雞蛋給家人吃並覺得自豪和獲得權力因為他們自己種植蔬菜養殖小雞就不再無助 , 不再依賴他人	they sell chicken eggs in refugee nutrients , they sell chicken eggs , they just eat their families , and they feel pride and receive power because they grow their own vegetable chickens , and they don't depend on others anymore .
這個方案在烏干達實施了給予前童軍一些心理上的幫助	this program was done in uganda , and it's done with some psychological help in the former child army .
實施這些方案讓他們重塑自我	it's implemented initiatives that allow them to reinvent themselves .
再一次 , 他們成為社會上的有用一員	and once again , they're socially useful .
我們也在監獄實施該計劃	we also implemented this program in prison .
所以現在沒時間實施更多的 " 根與芽 " 計劃	so there's no time for the roots and shoots to be built .
哦 , 他們也致力於艾滋病及其病毒方面的工作	oh , they're also working on hiv and their virus .
那是 " 根與芽 " 計劃非常重要的組成部分由大孩子跟小孩子談話	it's a crucial component of roots and shoots , and it's talked to kids .

藝術家戴安娜•科恩分享關於塑膠汙染對大海和我們日常生活嚴重影響的事實和一些想法 , 幫助大家來擺脫塑膠包圍圈 。	artist diana cohen is sharing the fact that plastic pollution is having a serious impact on the sea and some of our daily lives , helping people get out of the plastic surround .
consumerism , globalissues , green , missionblue , oceans , plastic	consumerism , global issue , greenee , mission bluee , plastic .
戴安娜•科恩diannacohen:關於塑膠汙染的嚴峻事實	diana cohen: the harsh truth about plastic pollution .
我是個視覺藝術家 , 也是塑膠汙染聯盟的創始人之一 。	i'm a visual artist and one of the founders of the plastic pollution coalition .
過去20年 , 我一直參與塑膠包的工作 , 我藝術創作的原材料是裁製和縫合塑膠 。	for the last 20 years , i've been working on plastic packets , so the raw materials that i've created are sanitations and sewage plastics .
讓塑膠變為平面和立體型藝術 , 雕塑和藝術裝置 。	it transforms plastic into print and threedimensional art , sculpture and art installation .
在與塑膠打交道的八年之後 , 我的一些作品開始開裂碎成許多小塑膠塊 。	after eight years of engaging with plastic , some of my work began to break into plastics and pieces .
我想 , " 好極了 。	i thought , " fantastic .
塑膠就像我們人類一樣短命 。 "	plastic is as short as human beings . "
我自學進一步深入瞭解塑膠 , 我的確瞭解到塑膠是個壞材料 。	i learned about plastic , and i did learn that plastic is a bad material .
塑膠碎成許多小塊 , 但它還是塑膠 , 這很糟糕 。	plastic breaks into lots of small patches , but it's still plastic , which is awful .
我們發現有很多塑膠漂浮於大海 。	we found a lot of plastic floating in the ocean .
然而在過去的幾年 , 我知道太平洋垃圾環流和垃圾漩渦 。	however , in the last few years , i've known the pacific garbage and the gyre .
我第一反應--我想這也是多數人的第一反應 , 知道這之後-- " 喔 , 我的上帝 !	and my first reaction i think that's the first reaction to most people , and after that " oh , my god !
我們要去那裡並清理這些塑膠 。 "	we're going there and cleaning up those plastics . "
所以我提議一隻貨船 , 兩隻退役拖網漁船 , 一臺起重機 , 一臺削片機和一臺冷壓機出海 。	so i proposed a cargo ship , two return trawlers , a crane , a shutter and a cold pressure machine .
我計劃是航行到垃圾環流帶 , 提高對於此汙染的高度重視 , 開始回收塑膠 , 切割它變成小片 , 然後冷壓變成塑膠塊 , 它可能被用來作為欠發達社群的建築材料 。	my plan was to sail to the garbage dump , raise high value on this pollution , to recycle the plastic , cut it into small chunks , cold compression into plastic , and it could be used as building materials for the community that owe it to .
我同那些曾去過垃圾環流帶的人們談過 , 他們也曾研究過塑膠汙染對海洋環境的汙染 , 交談之後 , 我開始意識到海上清理塑膠相比起全球每天產生塑膠的生產量就如大海撈針一樣 , 我必須回過頭想想 , 要展望更大的藍圖 。	i've been talking to people who've been to garbage loops , who've studied plastic pollution in the marine environment , and after talking , i've come to realize that cleaning up plastic is compared to the amount of plastic that's produced in the world around the globe as a needle in haystack , and i've got to go back and think about bigger blueprints .
真正的解決辦法就是:我們需要在源頭找到解決方法 。	and the real solution is this: we need to find solutions to the source .
我們需要切斷一次性使用塑膠和一次性塑膠的源頭 , 使得它們在全球範圍內每天不會再進入大海 。	we need to cut the sources of plastic , oneoff plastic , so that they don't enter the ocean every day on a global scale .
看看這個 , 我也知道我非常生氣 。	look at this , and i know that i'm very angry .
我並不只關心你也可能想象到的在太平洋中部我們現在所知的 , 權威資料是 , 11個垃圾塑膠環流帶 , 遍及世界五大海洋 。	and i'm not just concerned about what you might imagine in the middle of the pacific , what we now know , what authority data is , 11 trash plastic streams across the five oceans of the world .
我不僅僅是關心塑膠環流帶 , 也包括超市的塑膠包圍圈 。	i'm not just caring about plastic streams , but about supermarket plastic coils .
我要去超市 , 所有事物都是塑膠包裝 。	i'm going to the supermarket , and everything is plastic packaging .

我也關注在冰箱的塑膠 , 還有塑膠以及濾取塑膠的毒素被我們吃下和吸收到我們身體裡 。	i'm also concerned about plastic in the refrigerator , but also the plastics and the toxins that filter plastic from us eat and absorb ourselves .
我和其他的一群人們都關注這個塑膠汙染問題 , 組建了塑膠汙染聯盟 。	i and a bunch of other people are concerned about this plastic pollution problem , building a coalition for plastic pollution .
我們為解決這問題開始許多活動 , 它們中的一些是非常簡單的 。	we started solving lots of activity with these problems , and some of them are very simple .
其中一個是:在大海 , 我們發現百分80到百分90海洋廢棄物是塑膠 , 然後我們為什麼不稱其為:	one of them is that in the ocean , we find that 80 to 90 percent of the ocean waste is plastic , and why don't we call it ?
再迴圈 。 關於可持續和再迴圈的環保想法的書籍都是類似的觀點 。	loops . books about sustainable and recursive ideas are similar in ideas .
大家扔東西到垃圾桶裡 , 但是從來沒有再想過此事 。	people throw things in the trash cans , but never think about it again .
現實是什麼呢 ?	what is reality ?
在美國 , 塑膠垃圾回收率少於百分之七 。	in the united states , plastic waste rates are less than seven percent .
大家想實際看看 , 特別當塑膠變成塑膠瓶 , 絕大多數塑膠瓶僅被降級回收 , 或者焚燒 , 或運到中國 。	people want to see , especially when plastic is turned into a plastic bottle , the overwhelming majority of plastic bottles are recycled or burned or
當一個塑膠瓶可以被重製成一個塑膠瓶 , 或者重被使用時 , 正是被降級回收 , 使得塑膠瓶被製成小塑膠體 , 使得一個塑膠瓶不再被製成塑膠瓶回收利用 。	when a plastic bottle can be recreated into a plastic bottle , or when it's being reused , it's getting recycled and getting plastic bottles made into small plastic botles that no longer get reused to a plastic bottle .
對我們而言 , 這是個重大問題 。	it's a huge problem for us .
我們關注 , 並讓人們思考的另一件事是我們在原本3個r原則前 , reduce、reuse、recycle , 加了第四個r原則 , 它就是拒絕使用 。	the other thing that we got people thinking is that we reduce , reuse , recycle , three principles , and that's the fourth principle , which is rejection .
無論何時 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	whenever you refuse to use plastic and disposable plastics .
有替代品的使用 。 其中一些是非常老套 。	there are alternative uses . some of them are very oldfashioned .
我自己現在收集這些很酷的耐熱玻璃容器 , 使用這些而替換高興派和特百惠派塑膠容器來儲存食物 。	i myself am gathering these cool , turbotured glass vessels , using these replacing fundamentalists and luminous plastic vessels
我知道我這樣做有利於我自己和我的家庭 。	i knew i was doing it for myself and my family .
我們選擇使用不鏽鋼瓶和玻璃瓶是很容易的 , 你如果要出門 , 記得帶不鏽鋼瓶 , 讓它灌滿水 , 或者濾過水 , 而不要購買塑膠瓶裝水 。	we choose to use stainless stainless steel bottles and glass bottles easily , and if you go out and you remember rusty steel bottles , you filter it with water , or you don't buy plastic bottles of water .
我猜我想要告訴大家的是我知道你們大家關於此塑膠汙染知道得很多漂在大海上的塑膠是個嚴重的問題 , 但這是我們做為消費者自身產生的問題 , 我們也能自身解決這問題 。	i guess what i'd like to tell you about this plastic pollution that you all know about this is a serious problem in the ocean , but it's a problem that we've created as consumers , and we can solve it ourselves .
我們透過提高這問題的意識 , 教導人們選擇可替換性產品 , 能夠解決這問題 。	we're taught by raising our consciousness about solving the problem of alternative products .
所以無論何時 , 請選擇使用可替換性產品 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	so whenever you choose to use a replacement product , you refuse to use a onetime use of plastic and disposable plastic .
我們可以切斷源頭 , 阻止這塑膠汙染到我們的海洋裡 , 透過如上4r行動 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的家園 , 拯救我們自己 。	we can cut the source and stop the pollution in our ocean by , like fourrs , rescuing our oceans , rescuing ourselves , saving ourselves .

有一個問題我思考了很久 , 就是我們能否進化出一種第六感官 。 這種感官可以讓我們快速的便捷的獲得元資訊 , 或者是其他的一些資訊 , 在我們需要做出一些決定的時候 , 這些資訊能幫助我們做出正確的選擇 。	one of the questions that i've been thinking about for a long time is whether or not we can evolve a sixth senses , a sensory way of gaining dimension information , or other kinds of information , which can help us make the right choices when we're making decisions .
你們可能會說 , 當今的手機不正是如此嗎 ?	now , you might say , isn't that true ?
但是 , 我不認同 。	but i don't agree with that .
假設 , 當你在ted遇到某人 , ted , 毫無疑問 , 是每年最佳的社交場所 。 難道你會不跟人家握手 , 然後說: " 你能等一會嗎 ? 我要用手機google一下你 。 "	let's say when you meet someone at ted , ted , without a doubt , the best social space for annuals . why don't you shake someone's hand , and say , " can you wait a minute ? i'm going to google you on your phone . "
或者 , 當你在超市裡 , 站在一排巨大的貨架前 , 面對著各種各樣的廁紙 , 難道你會拿出手機 , 開啟瀏覽器登入一個網站 , 嘗試去決定到底哪一種廁紙才是最環保的 , 最應該買的 ?	or when you're standing in a supermarket range of giant shelves dealing with all kinds of toilet paper , or you take out your phone , and you turn on a website to try to decide which is the most ecological toilet paper , which should be the most purchased ?
所以說 , 我們並沒有一個便捷的渠道去獲取這些資訊 , 這些能幫助我們做出應該要幹什麼的最佳決定的資訊 。	so we don't have a convenient channel to get the information that's going to help us make the best decisions we should make .
因此 , 我的實驗室的研發團隊完成了一系列的發明 , 在不改變使用者行為的條件下 , 幫助使用者快速簡單的獲取這些資訊 。	so my r&amp ; d team in my lab completed a series of inventions without changing the user behavior , and helping the user to gather this information quickly .
現在 , 我將這個裝置展示給大家 。 這是我們至今最成功的版本 , 仍然在不斷改進 。	now , i'm showing this to you . this is the most successful version of our time . it's still improving .
我現在正佩戴著我們其實是把市面上常見的一些元件組裝在了一起 。 順便提一下 , 目前這個裝置的成本是350美元 。	i'm wearing now , actually , some of the components that we're seeing on the market , and by the way , the cost of this device is 350 dollars .
我佩戴著一個相機 , 就是一個簡單的網路攝像頭 , 一個便攜的用電池供電的投影儀和一個小鏡子 。	i'm wearing a camera with a simple webcam , a portable battery projector and a little mirror .
這些元件跟我口袋中的手機進行通訊 , 手機作為一個通訊和計算的裝置 。	these components communicate with my cell phone in my pocket as a communication and computation device .
畫面中 , 是我的天才學生pranavmistry , 他設計並製造了這整套系統 。	in this image , it was my genius student pranav mistry who designed and built this whole system .
我們可以看到 , 當他靠近任何表面時 , 資訊就會被投影到表面上 , 他就用雙手來進行操作 。	and what we see is that as he approaches any surface , the information is projected onto the surface , and he operates with his hands .

但當你想到你的朋友是長期的冒險活動時 , 因此 , 它是你為增加壽命和讓生命生機勃勃能夠做的最重要的事情謝謝	but when you think about your friends as a longterm adventure , therefore , it's the most important thing you can do to survive and enable living organisms to do . thank you .
能導電的墨水、一<unk>開關就由透明變不透明的窗戶、能播放音樂的果凍--這些東西確實存在 。 catarinamota說:現在是時候嘗試他們了 。 mota將帶領我們認識這些新穎和神奇的材料 , 她說 , 弄清楚這些材料的神奇之處的最好方式就是用它們來做實驗 , 不斷嘗試並樂在其中 。	and those inks that conduct electricity , having a thoroughty radio ink , fueled by transparency windows , zero jelly that actually exist . catarina mota says it's time to try them now . mota's going to take us on to understand these novel , miraculous materials , and she says that the best way to make clear these materials is to try and do experiments with them over and over again .
creativity , design , technology	we've got a lot of different things , and we've got to get away with that .

我有一位葡萄牙朋友 , 其祖父用一輛腳踏車和一臺洗衣機改裝成一輛汽車供家人乘用 。	i have a portuguese friend whose grandfather transformed with a bicycle and a washing machine into a car for his family .
他這樣做 , 一是因為他買不起車 , 但更重要的是因為他知道如何改裝汽車 。	and he did so because he couldn't afford a car , but more importantly , he knew how to modify a car .
曾經 , 我們都懂得一些機械的工作原理 , 也知道它們是怎麼製造出來的 , 所以我們能夠自己製作和維修它們.或者至少基於我們的瞭解作出明智的購買決定 。	once upon a time , we knew a few mechanical principles , and we knew how they were produced , so we could make and maintain them ourselves , or at least based on our understanding of the purchase decisions .
但我們很多這些diy的實用性技能在20世紀的下半葉就流失了 。	but a lot of these practical skills of diy were lost in the lower half of the 20th century .
但是現在 , 製作者社群和開放資源模式正在把這些物品的工作原理和製造材料的知識帶回到我們的生活中 。 而且我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個層面 , 也就是了解構成這些物品的元件 。	but now , the producer community and the opensource model is bringing this knowledge of the work of these objects and the manufacturing materials back into our lives , and i believe we need to bring that knowledge to the next level , the understanding of the components of the objects .
我們很多人都知道 , 像紙和織物這樣的傳統材料是什麼做成的 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。	many of us know what traditional materials like paper and fabric are made of , and how they are produced .
但是現在我們有了一些令人驚歎的未來複合材料-如可以變形的塑膠、可以導電的油漆、可以變色的顏料和可以發光的織物 。	but now we have some amazing clustering future composites , like transformable plastics , conductive paints , colorable fabrics .
下面讓我們來看一些新材料 。	let's look at some new materials .
這種導電墨水可讓我們 , 拋棄傳統的印刷電路板或電線的方法而直接用導電墨水來畫電路板 。	this conductive ink allows us to get rid of the traditional printed circuit board or wire methods that conduct electrical inks to draw circuit boards .
比如我手裡拿著的這個小裝置 , 是我們用導電墨水做成一個觸控性的感測器 , 一旦接觸人的皮膚 , 這個小燈就會亮起 。	so for example , this little device in my hand is a touch sensor that we use to make a touch sensor that's lit by contacting the skin of the people .
導電墨水已經被藝術家們應用到創作中了 , 最新的進展表明我們很快就能把它應用在鐳射印表機和鐳射筆中.	the conductive ink has been used by artists , and the latest progress is showing that we're going to be applying it in laser printers and lasers .
這是一張泡浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙.	this is a paper that was dipped in zero light , a sheet of acelene acid .
只浸過普通丙烯酸的紙只在其邊緣周圍有漫光現象 , 而這張浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙 , 當我們開燈時漫光會照亮整張紙.	immersed a regular paper with only a phenomenon of light around the edge , and immersed in this coloradopted , polyphilian , and when we turned on the light , illuminating the entire plastic sheet of paper .
就目前所知 , 這種材料已經被應用到室內設計和多點觸控系統兩個領域中了 。	as far as we know , this material has been applied in two areas of interior design and multitouch systems .
而熱變色顏料在特定的溫度下會改變顏色 。	and thermal color changes color at a specific temperature .
我先把這張東西放到一個電熱板上溫度設定比外界溫度稍高一點然後你可以看到發生了什麼.	i'm going to take this thing and put it on an electrical panel and set it up a little bit more temperature than the outside world , and you can see what happens .
除了其它用途 , 這種材料主要用作嬰兒奶瓶的製造 。 它能告訴你什麼時候瓶裡的東西涼到可飲用的溫度 。	in addition to the other uses , this material is mostly made out of baby bottles , and it's going to tell you when the bottle gets cold in the drinkable temperature .
這些就是我們通常所說的 " 智慧材料 " 的幾個例子 。	these are just a few examples of what we usually call " smart materials . "
幾年內 , 它們將被應用到很多我們日常使用的物件和科技產品上 。	within a few years , they will be applied to a lot of the objects and technological objects that we use every day .
我們也許還不會有科幻小說向我們保證的飛行汽車 , 但是我們能擁有隨溫度變色的牆 , 可以捲起來的鍵盤 , 和一<unk>開關就變不透明的窗戶 。	we may not yet have science fiction promised us for flying cars , but we can have walls that would be curled up with temperature , but we'll be able to open up a keyboard and we'll be able to open up a window into opaque temperatures .
我是科班出身的社會科學家 , 為什麼今天我在這裡講智慧材料 ?	i'm a social scientist from koban , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?
首先 , 我是個製造者 。	first of all , i'm a maker .
我對於東西如何運轉和怎樣製作有好奇心 , 我也相信我們應該對我們這個世界的組成材料有更深的瞭解 , 並且現在 , 我們對於這些構成我們未來的高科技材料瞭解不多 。	i'm curious about how things work and how they do things , and i believe that we should have a deeper understanding of the components of our world , and now we don't know very much about those hightech materials that make up our future .
要獲得少量的智慧材料是很難的 。	it's hard to get a handful of smart materials .
有關如何使用這些材料的資訊也很少 , 它們是如何製作的資訊就更加少得可憐 。	there's also a lot of information about how to use these materials , and there's a lot less information about how they're produced .
目前 , 它們絕大多數都存在於貿易機密和專利中 , 只有大學和大公司才能得到 。	right now , most of them are in trade secrets and patents only universities and large companies .
所以三年多以前 , 我和kirstyboyle發起了一個叫做openmaterials的專案 。	so over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i launched a project called open maternals .
在那個網站上 , 我們和想要加入我們的任何人 , 分享實驗 , 釋出資訊 , 鼓勵其他人為此作出力所能及的貢獻 , 並且收集像研究論文和像我們一樣的製造者所製作的教程一類的資源 。	on that website , we and everyone who wants to join us , experiments , sharing information , encouraging others to contribute to this effort and collect resources like research papers and the documents that produce like us .
我們希望把這一網站做成一個大規模的、集體生成的資料庫 , 蒐集用智慧材料diy的資訊 。	we wanted to take this website and make it a largescale , collective database to gather intelligent doityourself information .
但是我們為什麼要關心智慧材料是如何工作和它們是用什麼來製造的呢 ?	but why should we care about how smart materials work and what are they manufactured using ?
首先 , 因為我們無法影響我們不理解的東西 , 我們不理解和不會用的東西還會反過來影響我們 。	first , because we cannot influence what we don't understand , we don't understand and we don't use anything that will reverse us .
我們使用的東西 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活質量上產生深遠的影響 。	the things we use , the clothes we we wear , the houses we live in have profound impacts on our behavior , our health and the quality of life .
所以如果我們將要生活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界中 , 我們就應該知道並瞭解它們 。	so if we're going to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .
第二 , 同樣重要地 , 創新總是來源於修補匠 。	secondly , just as importantly , innovation is always the result of tinkerers .
很多時候 , 是業餘愛好者而非專家 , 發明和改進了諸如山地車、半導體、個人電腦、甚至飛機 。	in many cases , amateurs , not experts , invention and improvements things like mountains , semiconductors , personal computers , even airplanes .
材料科學的最大挑戰是它的複雜性 , 以及對昂貴的儀器的需求 。	the biggest challenge with material science is its complexity and its demand for expensive instruments .
但事實並非總如此 。	but that's not always the case .
伊利諾伊大學的兩名科學家在他們發表一篇關於用更簡便的方法制作導電墨水的論文時就明白了這個道理 。	two scientists at the university of illinois published a paper about conducting electrical inks in a simpler way .
jordanbunker在這一實驗之前是一個沒有任何化學經驗的人 。 他讀了這篇論文後在他的工作間裡用現成的物質和工具重複了這個實驗 。	jordan bunker on this experiment was a man who didn't have any chemical experience , and he read this essay and repeats this experiment with the materials and tools that he's developed in his workshop .
他用了一個烤箱 , 而且他甚至在另一個科學家/製造者的教程的基礎上自制了旋渦混合器 。	he took a oven , and he even made a vortex hybrid on the basis of another scientist/builder .
後來 , jordan在網上發表了他的實驗結果 , 包括所有他試過的沒成功的東西 , 這樣其他人可以學習然後複製這一實驗 。	later on , jordan published his results online , including all the unsuccessful things he tried so that others could learn and replicate the experiment .
所以jordan主要創新方式是拿一個在設施齊全的大學實驗室裡創造的實驗 , 然後在芝加哥的一個車庫裡用便宜材料和自制的工具來重複實驗 。	so jordan's main innovation was to take an experiment that was set up in a laboratory that was applied to approved in a garage in chicago using cheap materials and autonomous tools for experimentation .
在他發表的實驗結果基礎上 , 其他人可以接著做下去並且設計甚至更簡單的步驟和改進實驗 。	and based on the results that he published , others could follow it and design even simpler steps and improvements .
我想分享的另外一個例子她專案的目標是在突出材料富有表現力的特質的同時專注於製造者的創造力和製造技巧 。	another example i'd like to share with her is that she's focused on creativity and manufacturing skills at making makers .
電子工具在教我們東西如何運轉這方面非常有力 , 但是它們設計中傳承下來的約束影響我們學習的方式 。	electronic tools are very powerful in teaching us how things work , but the constraints that they pass through through that area affects how we learn .
所以hannah的方法 , 在另一方面 , 就是創制一系列的技術 , 來創造非常規的東西 , 透過教給我們材料本身的知識 , 把我們從事先設計好的約束中解放出來 。	so the hannah approach , on the other hand , is creating a series of techniques to create something very regular by teaching us about the materials themselves , freeing us from predetermined constraints .
在hannah眾多令人欽佩的試驗中 , 這個是我的最愛之一 。	this is one of my favorites in the experiments of hannah .
[ " 會說話的紙 " ]我們在這裡看到的只不過是一張紙上面的銅帶連線著一個mp3播放器和一塊磁鐵 。	[ " make you talk " ] what you're seeing here is just a piece of copper wiring a mp3 player and a magnet .
在麻省理工學院教授marcelocoelho研究的基礎上 , hannah使用各種材料創造了一系列紙質揚聲器 。 從普通的銅帶到導電的織物和墨水 ,	on the basis of marcelocoelho's research at mit , hannah used all kinds of materials to create a range of paper speakers , from ordinary copper to conductive fabric and ink .
就像jordan和其他很多製造者一樣 , hannah發表了她的配方並且允許任何人來重複這些實驗 。	like jordan and many other makers , hannah published her recipe and allowed anyone to run these experiments again .
但是紙上電子是材料科學中最有前景的分支之一 , 因為它讓我們能創造出便宜又靈活的電子產品 。	but paper is one of the most promising branches of material science , because it allows us to create cheap , flexible electronics .
所以hannah的手工作品 , 和她分享了她的發現這個事實 , 打開了一扇門 , 通向兼具美學和創新的一系列新的可能 。	so hannah's hands worked and shared her discoveries with her , opened the door to a new set of possibilities for beauty and innovation .
製造者的有趣之處在於我們創造是出於熱情和好奇 , 並且我們不害怕失敗 。	the interesting thing about makers is that we create passion and curiosity , and we're not afraid to fail .
我們通常從非傳統的角度處理問題 , 並且 , 在這個過程中 , 最終發現其他方案或者更好的方法 。	we tend to solve problems from a nonconventional perspective , and in the process , ultimately discovering alternatives or better ways .
所以當更多的人願意用新材料做試驗的時候 , 更多的研究者就會願意分享他們的研究成果 ; 有更多的製造商分享他們的知識 , 我們就會有更好的機會來創造造福我們所有人的科技 。	so when more people are willing to experiment with new materials , more researchers are willing to share their work ; with more manufacturers sharing their knowledge , we have a better chance of creating technology for all of us .
我的感覺有一點像tednelson在70年代初期的感覺一樣 , 他寫道 , " 你們現在必需懂電腦 。 "	i felt a little bit like a tednelson feeling in the early '70s , and he wrote , " you need to know computers now . "
那個時候 , 電腦是這些只有科學家關心的大型機 , 沒有人會夢想到放一臺在家裡 。	at the time , computers were these large machines that only scientists cared about , and nobody would ever dream of putting a family in their home .
所以我今天站在這裡說 " 你們現在必需懂智慧材料 " 有一點奇怪 。	so i'm standing here today and saying , " you need to know smart materials a little bit strange .
請記住對於新興科技擁有先發制人的知識是確保我們在對未來的創造中有發言權的最好方式 。	keep in mind that having primary knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to make sure that we have a say in the creation of the future .
當我們開車是 , 我們就坐進了一個玻璃氣泡中 , 鎖上門 , 踩下油門 , 依靠眼睛為我們自己導航 。 即使我們僅僅只能看見車前車後的幾輛車 。 但是假如汽車能互換關於位置、速度的資料 , 並運用預測模型來為每一位司機測算最安全的線路呢 ? 詹妮佛海麗構想了一個零車禍的世界 。	and as we drive by that , we're going to be sitting in a glass bubble , locking the door , pressing the gas door , and navigating ourselves with our eyes , even if we just see a few cars behind the car , but what if cars were exchanged for different locations , speeds and predicted models for every driver's safest route ? jenniferry set up a zero world ?
詹妮弗海麗:汽車若能交流車禍或可避免	jennifer hay: cars can be in a traffic james car accidents or preventable .
讓我們來面對一樁事實吧開車是一件危險的事	so let's face it: driving is a dangerous thing .
它是我們不願意去想的事物之一但事實上那些神像和平安符世界各地都有人把它們擺在儀表盤的上方這就無意中透露出一個我們都心知肚明的事實	it's one of the things that we don't want to think about , but the truth is that the divine peace is peaceful all over the world , and people are putting it on top of the dashboard , which inadvertently reveals a fact that we all know .
車禍是死亡的主因尤其在美國16到19歲的美國人群中死亡的主因並且百分之七十五的車禍都與毒品和酒精無關	car accidents are the cause of death , especially in the united states between the ages of 16 and 19 , and 75 percent of all deaths from drugs and alcohol .
沒人能給出確切答案但我記得我第一次出車禍	no one could give the exact answer , but i remember my first time in a car accident .
我當時還是個開車的新手 , 當時正在外面高速路上開著車 。 我突然看見我前面汽車的剎車燈亮了	i was a new car and i was driving , and i was driving , and i suddenly saw the brake lights in front of me on the outside .
我當時想好吧他減速了那我也減速好了	and i thought , okay , he's slowed down , and i'm slowing down .

但是我前面那個人並不是在減速	but the man in front of me wasn't slowing down speed .
他停車了突然停車在高速路上突然停車	he parked , and he parked , and he stopped at the highway , and he stopped .
速度從65邁瞬降到0	it went from 65 to zero .

我當時感覺到我的車的防抱死系統啟動了但車還在行駛並沒停下來的意思我也知道我的車停不了了安全氣囊也鼓了起來車報廢了但幸運的是沒有人受傷	i felt the car was launched , but the car was still running , and i knew that my car was not stopping , and the airbags were there that was wiping out , but fortunately no one was hurt .
但我根本不知道我前面那輛車要停而且我想我們可以比那做得更好	but i didn't know that i was going to stop in front of me , and i thought we could do better than that .
我想我們透過實現 " 讓汽車之間對話 " 來改變我們的駕駛體驗	i think we've made it happen by changing our experience of driver's dialogue between the cars .
我希望你們能思考片刻思考一下現在的駕駛體驗是怎麼樣的	i want you to think for a minute about how the present driving experience looks like .

對吧 ? 你只能靠雙眼來導航	right ? you can navigate with your eyes .
對你別無他法眼睛並非是用來幹著活兒的但是有些事情你就必須得做 , 比方說 , 你想換個車道那你第一件要做的事是什麼	it's not something you're used to doing survival work , but something you have to do , for example , you want to change a lane , it's what you're going to do the first thing you want to do .
將眼睛從車道上移開對	take the eyes out of the lanes .

所有人都這麼做這是安全的駕駛方式	and that's what everybody else does , and it's a safe way to drive .
我們為什麼這麼做 ? 因為我們別無選擇我們必須作出一個抉擇是朝這兒看還是朝那兒看	why are we doing this , because we don't have the choice , because we have to make a decision that looks like it or that way .

汽車是三維物體位置速度都是固定的	cars are threedimensional objects at a fixed rate .
行使在路上的時候	it's the way it's going to happen .

貝基布蘭頓計劃在一年裡就在他的小貨車裡住並且遊歷全國 , 但是當沮喪加劇而且自由作家的工作泡湯的時候 , 他的旅營就變成了無家可歸了 。 在這個溫馨的演講中 , 她描述了她作為美國無家可歸的工作者之一的獨特經歷 。	the becky brandton project lives in his van for a year and goes around the country , but when the frustration bubbles and freelance writers became homeless , and in this beautiful speech , she describes the unique experience of being homeless as an american worker .

貝基布蘭頓:我無家可歸的一年	becky brandton: my homeless year .
我是一個作家 , 一個新聞記者 , 我也是一位具有強烈求知慾的人 。 所以在做新聞記者的22年裡 , 我知道了很多新奇的事物 。	i'm a writer , a journalist , and i'm also a strongly appealing person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned a lot about the strange things .
而三年前 , 我學會做的一件事就是變成隱形人 。	and three years ago , one of the things i learned to do was to become invisible .
我成了一個無家可歸的工作者 。	i became a homeless worker .
我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作在我父親那年二月去世之後我決定去旅行	i quit my newspaper editor's job , and after my father died in february of that year , i decided to travel .
他的去世對我打擊非常大 。	his death struck me very big .
當時這麼做 , 是因為有很多我想去感知和處理的事 。	it's doing that because there's a lot of things i want to perceive and receive .
旅遊時我天天都在露營 。 並且決定在休旅車裡住一年就當作是一段長期野營旅行 。	i camped every single day while traveling and decided to live in a suspension vehicle for a year period of time .
所以 , 我就帶上我的貓 , 我的羅特威爾犬和露營的裝備裝載到1975產的雪佛萊旅遊車上 , 開車去看日落但當時完全沒想過三件嚴重的事	so i brought in my cat , my rotwell and camp equipment , to the 1975 chevy ride in chevy , driving to the sunset , but had no idea of the three serious things .
一:社會將住房即使是很小的房間 , 和人的價值等同起來 。	one: social housing equals human value , even a tiny room .
二:我沒有意識到其他人的負面言語對我們本身的影響是多麼嚴重 , 假如我們放任不管 。	two: i didn't realize how negative verbal responses are to our influence , if we let go of it .
三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種生活態度而不是一種生活方式 。	three: i didn't realize that homelessness was a lifestyle , not a lifestyle .
一開始 , 住在車裡是很不錯的 。	initially , it's pretty good to be living in a car .
我在露天洗澡 , 正常的去外面吃東西 。	i was showering up , and i was just going out and eating things .
而且有時間去抒發情感 。	and it's also time to channel our emotions .
但是後來 , 因我父親去世而帶來的悲憤和痛沮開始加劇 。	but then the anger and the depression that my father died began to intensify .
我自由作家的工作結束了 。 我就需要去找一件全職工作來支付我的賬單 。	my freelance writer's job ended , and i needed to find a fulltime job to pay my bills .
從一個非常溫和的春天變到一個極其炎熱的夏天會怎樣呢 。	what happens when we go from a very gentle spring to a very hot summer .
不管車停在哪都是難以忍受的不用說也很明顯我帶著一隻貓和一隻狗 , 而且非常的熱 。	it doesn't matter if the car parks anywhere can't say it's obvious that i'm wearing a cat and a dog and it's very hot .
貓從車窗來回的跑 。	the cat runs back and forth from the window of the car .
狗跑到了狗狗護理中心 。	the dog went to a dog nurse .
不管什麼時候 , 只要可以 , 我就會去用在辦公大樓和卡車車站裡員工用的淋浴 。	whenever i can , i'm going to use my office buildings and truck stops for showers .
或者在公共衛生間裡洗洗 。	or washing it in public health .
在夜裡車裡的溫度很少會降到華氏80度以下 , 這使我幾乎無法入睡 。	the temperature in the car in the night rarely drops below 80 degrees fahrenheit , which makes me almost impossible to sleep .
食物在高溫下腐壞 。	food rotted in temperature .
冷藏櫃裡的冰幾個小時就化完了 , 非常苦悶的時期 。	the ice in the locker was finished for hours , and it was a very painful period .
我沒錢找公寓 , 或者找不到讓我可以養狗和貓的地方 。	i had no money to find apartments , or i couldn't find a place where i could raise dogs and cats .
我不想把它們拋棄 。 所以我繼續待在旅行車裡 。	i didn't want to give them up . so i kept on going in the van .
但炎熱的天氣使我飽受折磨以至於在夜裡走50英尺到車外面的公共衛生間都懶的動 。 我用桶和垃圾袋當廁所 。	but thermal weather made me so suffering that i could get 50 feet out of the night and be lazy in the outhouse of public health . i used a bucket and a garbage bag as a toilet .
當冬天來臨的時候 , 溫度驟降到零度以下 。 然後就一直這麼冷 。	the winter came in , the temperatures came down below zero and it stayed that cold .
我又遇到了一堆新問題 ,	i've got a bunch of new questions .
每晚我的車都停在不同的地方 。 這樣才可以不讓警察發現以至於和警察爭吵 。	i parked in different locations every night so i could not get the police to see the argument as much as fighting with the police .
當然 , 並不是每次都成功 。	of course , it wasn't always successful .
但是 , 我覺得我已無力掌控自己的生活了 。	but i felt like i was in control of my life .
我也不知道什麼時候或者是如何發生的 , 我這麼快就從一個有才的寫手 , 新聞從業者變成一個無家可歸 , 住在車裡的女人這簡直是快的難以置信 。	i didn't know what was happening or how it happened , and i was rapidly going from being a talented writer to journalist to being a homeless woman living in a vehicle , which is just unbelievable .
我並沒有變 。 我的智商沒有降低 。	i didn't change . my iq didn't go down .
我的才能 , 我的正直 , 我的價值 , 所有關於我的這些東西都還是一樣 。	my talent , my integrity , my value , everything about me is the same .
但是從某種程度上 , 我還是改變了 ,	but in a way , i changed again .
我越來越沮喪 , 像一個漩渦一樣不斷地往下沉 。	i'm getting frustrated , like a whirl eddy , going down and sinking .
後來有人介紹我去一個專為無家可歸之人開的健康診所 。	later on , i was introduced to a health clinic that was dedicated to homeless people .
我去了 。 我有三天都沒有洗澡了 ,	i went . i did not bathe for three days .
我和其他那些排隊的人一樣沮喪 , 身上的味道也很難聞 。	i was just as depressed as all those other lines of people , and my body was smelling hard .
我只是沒有喝醉或者興奮 。	i was just not drunk or excited .
當一些無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括一個以前在大學任教的教授 , 他們說: " 你不是無家可歸 , 你真正在這裡的原因是什麼 ? "	when people were homeless , they realized , including a former professor at the university , that they said , " you're not homeless . what's the reason why you're here ? "
其他的無家可歸的人不把我當作是無家可歸的人看待 。 但是我自己是這麼認為的 。	other homeless people view me as if i'm homeless , but i myself think of it .

到底我們需要怎麼樣的世界	what kind of world do we need ?

這對已有世界秩序行得通嗎 ?	is this going to work in the world order ?

在我們的種族中 , 男人們定義現實然後逼迫他人接受現實遵守規則	in our species , men define reality and force others to accept reality and follow the rules .
規則常常發生變化 , 但總是對男性有益就這樣 , 在一致遵循的狀況下在經濟上並不成立的規則卻完美地存在	the rules are constantly changing , but they always benefit men , and in the circumstances that are consistent , the rules are perfectly available in the economy .
從上到下 , 一層層的力量濫用	from top to bottom , a layer of force abuse .

即使是最一無所有的男人也有人被他凌虐常常是婦女或者兒童	even the most destitute of men and men have someone abused , often a woman or a child .
我再也受不了少數人操縱多數人透過性別 , 收入 , 種族和階級的手段	i'm fed up with the power that a few people can operate by gender , by income , by race and by class .

在一個倫敦那麼大的城市裡 , 每天都要消耗掉三千萬噸糧食 。 但是 , 這些食物都從何而來 ? 建築師carolynsteel探討每天餵養一個城市的神話 , 介紹古代的食物運輸如何影響城市的形成和發展 。	in a city the size of london , 30 million tons of food every day , but where do they come from ? carolyn steel look at the myth of feeding a city on a daily basis and introducing how ancient food transportation has impacted the formation of the city .

越來越多的這些地貌不只是生產食物養活我們	more and more of these landscapes aren't just producing us food .
隨著我們越來越多人移居城市越來越多人吃肉所以每年全球有三分之一的糧食現在是用來餵動物而不是餵養我們人類	as more and more of us move to cities , more and more people are now eating meat , so a third of the global food every year is now feeding animals rather than feeding us humans .

這是大西鐵路在1840的照片	this is a photograph of the west circuit in 1840 .

這些改變了一切	and that changed everything .
首先 , 他第一次使城市成長變成了可能不論地點、成為什麼規模和形狀的城市	first , he had grown the city for the first time , possibly no matter where it was , what scale and shaped the city .

mit研究人員斯凱拉•蒂比茨從事自我裝配的研究一個取代建造東西的主意 , 我們能創建制作自己的材料 , 很像dna鏈打包的方式 。 目前還是一個巨大概念的早期階段 ; 蒂比茨向我們展示了三個還在實驗中的專案 , 我們可以一窺一個自我裝配的未來可能的樣子 。	instead of the idea of selfgenerating , mit researcher kiracladia researcher , where we can create the materials that we build , much like the way dna chains are packed in early stages ; tibitz is showing us three projects that still have them , and we can peer into a future where we can have a selfassemble .

我相信很快我們的建築和機器將能自我組裝 , 自我複製和自我修復 。	i believe soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , selfreplication and selfrepair .
因此我要向各位展示我所認為的製造業的當前狀況 , 接著再將其與一些自然系統比較 。	so i'm going to show you what i think of as the manufacturing industry , and then compare it to some natural systems .
那麼在當前的製造業中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 50萬至上百萬個部分 , 非常複雜 , 使用了在鋼鐵 , 混凝土和玻璃方面的新技術 。	so in the current manufacturing industry , we have a skyscraper for two and a half years , half a million to a million , very complicated , using new technologies for concrete and glass .
我們有令人激動的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年時間 , 兩百五十萬個部分 。	we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years , 2 . 5 million parts .
但另一方面 , 如果看看自然系統 , 我們有擁有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 能在一萬納秒內摺疊起來 , 我們能在大約一小時內對帶有三十億鹼基對的dna進行復制 。	but on the other hand , if you look at the natural system , we have two million types of proteins that can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , and we can reconstruct our dna with about 3 billion base pairs in about an hour .
這就是我們自然系統的複雜性 , 但它們非常高效 , 比我們建造的任何東西都要高效 , 比我們能建造的任何東西都要複雜 。	it's the complexity of our natural systems , but they're very efficient , more efficient than anything we build , more sophisticated than anything we can build .
它們在能源方面更加高效 。	they're more efficient in terms of energy .
它們很少犯錯 。	they make very few mistakes .
他們能自我修復保持長壽 。	they can repair their longevity self .
關於自然系統有件超級有意思的事情 。	something really interesting about the natural system .
如果我們能將其轉換為我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們構建事物的方式就會有很大的潛力 。	if we can convert it to our built environment , then there's a lot of potential in the way we construct things .
我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。	i think the key to this is selfassembly .
如果我們想要在自身的身體環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。	if we want to harness our selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there are four key factors .
第一個是 , 我們需要解碼我們所要建造的東西的所有的複雜度也就是我們的建築和機器 。	the first is that we need to decode all the complexity of what we're building and machinery .
我們需要把它們解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們的建築運作的dna 。	we need to decode it into simple sequences that are basically the dna of how our buildings work .
接著我們需要可程式設計的部分這部分能接受這一序列並用於摺疊或是重塑 。	and then we need programmable parts that can take this sequence and fold it or reshap it .
我們需要一些能量來進行啟用 , 使我們的這些部分能夠依照程式摺疊起來 。	we need some energy for the launch , so that we'll be programmed to fold it .
我們需要一些型別的糾錯冗餘以保證我們成功建造的就是我們想要的 。	we need some error redundancy to ensure that what we're successful in is what we want .
因此 , 我要向各位展示一些我和我的同事正在進行的要實現這種自我組裝的未來的專案 。	so i'm going to show you some projects that my colleagues and i are working on to realize this selfassembly future .
頭兩個專案是macrobot和decibot 。	the first two projects are macrobot and decibot .
這些專案都是大規模可重構機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。	these projects are largescale reconstructing robots at eight feet , 12 feet of protein .
它們嵌入機電裝置 , 感測器 。	they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .
你需要把想要摺疊的方式解碼成 , 解碼成一系列角度負120度 , 負120度 , 0度 , 0度 , 120度 , 負120度 , 這類的東西 ; 一系列角度 , 或轉向 , 可以用電線把這個次序傳過去 。	you need to decode the way you want to fold it into a series of angles of minus 120 , minus 120 degrees , zero zero , zero , 120 degrees , negative 120 degrees , these kinds of things ; a series of angles , or transformations , that can transmit this sequence by wire .
每個單元獲取自己的訊息比如負120.它進行旋轉 , 檢查是否旋轉到位然後把序列傳給它的鄰居 。	each unit captures its message— such as negative 120 . it rotates , checks if it rotates to its neighbor .
有許多傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師為這個專案工作 。	there are some remarkable scientists , engineers , designers working on this project .
我認為這一專案真的揭示出:這真的可擴充套件麼 ?	and i think this project really reveals: is this really expandable ?
我是說 , 花費數千美元許多人時來製造這個八英尺的機器人 。	i mean , it cost thousands of dollars to build this eightfoot robot .
我們真的能擴大它麼 ? 我們真的能在每個部分中都嵌入機器人麼 ?	can we really expand it ? can we really embed the robots in every single part ?
下一個問題是看看被動性 , 或被動地嘗試讓重組具有可程式設計性 。	the next question is looking at passiveness , or passively trying to make recombination programmable .
但它更進了一步 , 它嘗試進行實際計算 。	but it goes a step further , and it tries to do actual calculation .
基本上嵌入了多數計算的基礎構建模組 , 數字邏輯閘 , 直接進入各個部分 。	basically embedded in the building blocks of most calculations , the digital logic gates going straight into all parts .
這是與非門 。	it's the opposite .
每個要用於計算的門上都有一個四面體 , 有兩個輸入四面體 。	each of these calculated doors has a tetrahedron , and two inputs .
其中一個是來自使用者的輸入 , 就像你在構建磚塊 。	one of them is the input from the user , just like you're building bricks .
另一個是來之前前放好的一塊磚的輸入 。	the other one was the previous input of a brick before .
接著它會給出三維空間的輸出 。	and then it exports to threedimensional spaces .
這意味著使用者以他們想要的方式堆砌磚塊 。	it means that the users build bricks in the way they want to .
它依據之前所做的和你的指令進行計算 。	it calculates on the basis of what you've done and what you've commanded .
現在它開始在三維空間內移動上或者下 。	and now it starts moving up and down in three dimensions .
看左面 , [1 , 1]的輸入等於0輸出 , 表示向下 。	look at the left , [1 , 1] input is equivalent to 0 output , which goes down .
在右邊 , [0 , 0]的輸入是1輸出 , 表示向上 。	on the right , [0 , 0 , 0] input is output , 1 output goes up .
因此這真正的的意味是我們的結構中現在包含了我們想要構建的藍圖 。	so what this really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints that we want to build .
因此關於想要構建的事物的資訊已經全部嵌入其中 。	so the information about building something is fully embedded .
這意味著我們有了某種形式的自我複製 。	it means that we have some form of selfreplication .
對這種情況 , 我稱之為自我導向複製 , 因為你的結構中包含了精確的藍圖 。	in this case , i call it selfdirected replication , because you have exactly the exact blueprints in your structure .
如果遇到錯誤 , 你可以替換一個部分 。	if you're confronted with errors , you can change parts .
所有的本地資訊都嵌入其中 , 告訴你如何修復它 。	all of the local information is embedded in it , telling you how to fix it .
因此你有個可以攀爬的東西 , 能讀出它並一個一個的輸出 。	so you have something that climbs , reads it and outputs it .
它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部指令輸入 。	it's directly embedded ; there's no external command input .
我要展示的最後一個專案名為偏心鏈條 , 它可能是我們現在看到的被動自我裝配系統中最令人激動的例子 。	the last project i'm going to show is called biases , and it's probably the most exciting example of the passive selfassembly system that we're seeing right now .
它具有可重構性和可程式設計性使它成了為了一個完全地被動系統 。	it's reconstructive and programmable , and it's made it available for a completely passive system .
基本上就是你有了一連串的元素 。	it's basically a series of elements that you have .
每個元素都是完全相同的 , 且它們是偏心的 。	each element is identical , and they're preferred .
每個鏈條 , 或每個元素想要向右轉或是向左轉 。	every chain , or every element , wants to turn right or left .
如果你要裝配鏈條 , 需要為它程式設計 。	if you are going to assemble chains , you have to program it .
要告訴每個單元是要左轉還是右轉 。	to tell the unit whether it's left or right .
當你搖動這個鏈條時 , 它就摺疊起來程式設計你所為它編碼的任何結構因此這種情況下 , 一個螺旋體 , 火這種情況 , 兩個相連的立方體 。	when you shake this chain , it originates to the program which you encode for , so in this case , a spiral , fire , two cubes connected .
基本上你可以在三維空間內程式設計或是一維、二維這鏈條是完全被動的 。	you're programming in three dimensions or onedimensional , twodimensional chains that are completely passive .
這向我們預示了怎樣的未來呢 ?	what's the future that's introduced to us ?
我認為這告訴我們這些在我們的身體結構、我們的建築和機器中這種自我裝配、自我複製和自我修復的可能性 。	i think what this tells us is that these are the possibilities for selfreplication , selfreplication and selfrepair in our physical structure , our architecture and machines .
在這些部分中有新的可程式設計性 。	there's new programmability in these parts .
從中你能獲得計算的新可能性 。	you get new possibilities for computing .
我們將有空間計算 。	we'll have spatial computation .
想象一下我們的建築、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都能進行實際計算 。	imagine our buildings , our bridges , our machines all running a practical computation .
多麼令人驚奇的平行計算和分散式計算能力和新的設計可能性啊 。	what an amazing parallel computing and distributed computing and the possibility for design .
這是項令人激動的潛力 。	it's a very exciting potential .
我認為這些我向各位展示的專案僅僅是邁向未來的一小步 , 如果我們為一個新的自我組裝的世界實現了這些新技術的話 。	i think these projects that i've shown you are just a small step towards the future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembly world .
我們已踏上過月球 , 我們已測繪了大陸 , 我們甚至已去過海底最深處--兩次 。 還剩下什麼值得我們的下一代去探索 ? 生物學家和內森•沃爾夫提出了這樣的答案:幾乎所有事物 。 " 我們可以從那小到看不見的世界開始 " , 他說 。	we've stepped on the moon , we've mapped the continent , we've even been to the bottom twice . what's the last generation to explore ? biologists and nathan wolf have given the answer: almost everything . we can start with that tiny little world , " he said .
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	so , you've got dievers , you're essential for life .
內森•沃爾夫:還有什麼值得探索 ?	nathan wolf: what else is it ?
最近我去了威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市 。	i was recently in belloyd , wisconsin .
我去那裡是為了紀念一名20世紀的探險家 , 羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯 。	i went there to commemorate the 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .
當他在美國自然歷史博物館的時候 , 安德魯斯領導了一系列對未知領域的探險 , 比如說在這裡的戈壁灘 。	as he was at the us natural history museum , andrews led a series of expeditions to the unknown , like here in the gobill beach .
他是個了不起的人物 。	he was an incredible figure .
他後來據說是印第安娜瓊斯角色的原型 。	he's been told by the prototypes of indiana jones characters .
當我在威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市的時候 , 我給一群中學學生上了一堂公開課 。	when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i took a public class for a bunch of middle school students .
我現在想告訴你們 , 如果真的有什麼比在ted做演講還難的話 , 那就是嘗試保持他們的注意力一群上千個12歲的孩子 , 並保持45分鐘 。	i'm going to tell you now that if it's harder than giving a talk at ted , that's trying to keep their attention in front of a thousand 12yearolds and keep your 45 minutes .
在我講完之後 , 他們問了很多問題 , 但有一個讓我自始至終難以忘記 。	after my talk , they asked a lot of questions , but one that made me hard to forget .
有個小女孩站起來 , 問了一個問題: " 我們該去哪裡探索呢 ? "	and a little girl stood up and asked the question , " where do we explore ? "
我想我們中的絕大多數有種觀念 , 那就是 , 地球上的大探索時代已經結束 , 我們的下一代人應該去外太空或者海洋最深處從而去尋找值得探索的東西 。	i think that the vast majority of our ideas are that the age of exploration on earth is over , that our next generation should go to space or the deepest in the ocean and seek things worth exploring .
但真的是這樣嗎 ?	but is that really what ?
真的沒有重要的地方留給我們探索了嗎 ? 整個地球上都沒有 ?	is there really no important space left for us to explore ? there isn't a whole earth ?
這讓我回憶起我最喜歡的生物領域的探險家之一 。	this reminds me of one of my favorite biological domains .
他是位未知世界的探索家 , 馬丁努斯•威廉•拜耶林克 。	he's an explorer of the unknown world , martinus william billyn .
拜葉林克當初想找出引起菸草花葉病的原因 。	and what bleef linker was trying to do was find a cause of tobacco leaf disease .
他提取了受過感染的菸草汁液 , 然後讓這些汁液經過一層比一層更細的過濾 。	he extracted an infected tobacco sap , and he let the sap go through a filter that's more nuanced than one layer .
他得出一個結論 , 剩下的裡面一定有什麼東西它們比那時最小的已知的生命形態--細菌 , 還要小 。	he came to the conclusion that something was left in there that was smaller than what was known as the smallest form of life bacteria .
他給這個神秘的東西起了個名字	he gave a name to this mysterious thing .
叫它們 , 病毒在拉丁文裡是 " 毒藥 " 的意思 。	call them a virus in latin for " poison . "
在發現病毒之後 , 拜耶林克為我們打開了一個全新的世界 。	after the discovery of viruses , bayelink opened a whole new world for us .
我們現在知道病毒構成我們星球上絕大部分的遺傳資訊超過所有其他生命的遺傳資訊的總和 。	we now know that viruses make up most of the genetic information on our planet more than the sum of all other life .
而且顯然已經出現了無數有關病毒的切實應用在這個世界上--像天花的根除 , 子宮癌的疫苗的降臨--我們現在知道它大部分是由乳頭瘤病毒引起的 。	and obviously there have been countless applications for viruses in the world things like the eradication of smallpox , a uterus cancer descended we now know that it's mostly caused by sarcoma .
而且拜耶林克的發現可不是500年前的事情 。	and baillynker's findings weren't 500 years ago .
拜耶林克發現病毒這件事也就發生於100多年前 。	billynker found out about the virus more than 100 years ago .
也就是說當汽車都已經出現在世的時候 , 我們還不知道這種構成了我們星球上大部分的遺傳資訊的生物 。	that means that when cars are on the earth , we still don't know that's the vast majority of genetic information beings that constitute our planet .
我們現在有些很了不起的工具來幫助我們探索未知世界 , 像基因深度測序 , 可以讓我們不只是停留在表面來看自某個特定物種的獨立基因組 , 而是研究整個基因組--我們身體裡面和周邊無處不在的微生物群落 , 並且記錄下這些物種的遺傳資訊 。	we now have some incredible tools to help us explore the unknown world , the depth of the gene , to allow us not just to remain on the surface and look at the independent genome of a particular species , but to study the entire genome the entire genome that our bodies and microbial communities that live in and around us , and to document the genetic information of those species .
我們可以應用這些技術來研究從土壤到皮膚和它們中間的一切 。	we can use these techniques to study everything between soil and skin and everything in between .
在我所在的機構裡面 , 我們現在經常這麼做 , 來尋找暴發的原因 , 那些我們還不清楚的原因.	in my own institutions , which we're doing a lot , to look for riots , things that we don't know yet .
稍微給你們講下這是怎麼做的 , 想象下從你們每個人那裡取一個鼻腔分泌物標本	i'm going to tell you a little bit about how it works , so i'm just going to take a nasal secret library from each of you and every one of you .
像這種事是我們經常做的 , 為了尋找呼吸道病毒 , 像流行性感冒病毒 。	things like these are things that we often do to find respiratory viruses like influenza .
我們首先看到的是海量的遺傳資訊 。	the first thing we're seeing is mass genetic information .
如果我們開始仔細看看這些遺傳資訊 , 我們會看到一些常見的資訊當然了 , 有很多人類的遺傳資訊 , 但也有很多細菌和病毒的資訊 , 大部分是你鼻子裡面完全無害的東西 。	if we start looking at the genetic information , we're going to see some common information , of course , with a lot of human genetic information , but also a lot of bacteria and viruses , mostly things that are completely harmless in your nose .
但我們也會看到一些非常非常讓人吃驚的東西 。	but we also see some very , very surprising things .
當我們開始研究這些資訊 , 我們會發現你鼻子裡面20%的遺傳資訊跟我們所見過的東西--任何植物 , 動物 , 真菌或者細菌 , 都對不上號 。	when we started looking at this information , we found that 20 percent of the genetic information you had in your nose was in any plant , any plant , any fungus , any bacteria , any bacteria .
我們基本上對這些一無所知 。	we're essentially ignorant of those .
我們這裡的一小部分研究這些資料的人們 , 稱呼這些資訊為生物暗物質 。	a small number of people here who studied this data , we call it biological dark matter .
我們知道以前從未見過這些生物暗物質 ; 這似乎可以被稱之為我們自己遺傳資訊裡的未知大陸 。	we know that these biological dark matters have never been seen before ; it seems to be called the unknown continent of our own inheritance .
而且數量非常之多 。	and that's a lot .
如果你認為你鼻子裡面20%的遺傳資訊有很多生物暗物質 , 那當我們看你內臟的時候 , 那有將近40%到50%的生物暗物質 。	if you think that there's a lot of biological dark matter in your nose 20 percent of your genetic information , when we look at your gut , that's close to 40 to 50 percent of your biological dark matter .
即使在相對無菌的血液裡 , 也有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質--無法被歸類 , 無法被判別類別 , 跟我們所見過的東西都不同 。	even in the relatively sterile blood , one to two percent of the information is dark matter can't be categorized , can't be judged , can't be judged , can't be judged , can't be judged .
開始我們以為這是人為的東西 。	to start with what we thought was a human thing .
這些基因深度測序工具相當比較新 。	these genes are relatively new .
但當它們變得越來越來精確 , 我們認為這些資訊是一種新的生命 , 或者至少某一部分是種生命 。	but as they become more and more accurate , we think that information is a new form of life , or at least a section of it is a new form of life .
即使這些關於解釋生物暗物質的存在的假設還處於嬰兒期 , 一個讓人非常非常激動的可能性存在著:那就是藏在這個生命裡面 , 在這些遺傳資訊裡 , 有一種沒有被識別的生命的標識 。	even though these hypotheses about the existence of biological dark matter are still infant moments , a very , very thrilling possibility exists: that is , in this life , a mark of life that is not identified .
當我們探索這些一串串a/t/c/g嘌呤的時候 , 我們也許會發現全新的生命 , 就像拜耶林克 , 從根本上改變我們對生物學特性的理解 。	as we explore these strings of a/c/c/g purine xeroids , we may find a whole new life , like bayerink , fundamentally changing our understanding of biology .
這也許會讓我識別出困擾我們的某種癌症的原因 , 或者識別出我們不熟悉的疾病暴發的根源 , 或者創造出一種分子生物學的新工具 。	it might make me recognize some of our cancers or identify the origins of a disease that we're not familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .

那麼太陽系--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式--是如何獲取這樣一個與宇宙其他部分的特殊關係的呢 ?	so the solar system our environment , in our form how do we get a special relationship with the rest of the universe ?
stephenhawking觀點中其中一個正確面--我的意思是 , 這是正確的 , 但是著重點是錯的 。 其中一個正確面是它並沒有倚賴任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟發生 。 它的發生只依賴於我們現在富有的三種東西 。	there's one side of stephen hawking i mean , that's right , but it's right , but it's wrong , and one of the right things is that it doesn't depend on any special physics , no special amenity , no miracles , no magic happening , it just depends on three things that are now rich .
其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理需要計算 , 計算需要電腦--現有的知識下不可能不需要物質來製造電腦 。	one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing that requires computation , computational processing , computational requirements that computers currently knowledge cannot be materialized to make computers .
我們還需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 要使得用來記錄我們所發現知識的媒介工作 。	we also need energy to make computers , and most importantly , to document the mediums that we've discovered .
