我們的環境中充滿了證據 。	our environment is full of evidence .
但是我們常常忽略了測試--比如 , 牛頓的地球引力定律--大約是在300年前提出的 。	but we often ignore tests let's say , newton's law of gravity , about 300 years ago .
但是我們習以為常的證據 , 從數十億年前就在地球上的每個角落裡不斷墜落 , 也會在接下來的數十億年裡繼續墜落 。 其他科學也同樣如此 。	but we're used to thinking about the proof that we've been collapsing everywhere on the planet since billions of years , and we've been falling down over the next billion years , and so do all the sciences .
就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學大部分基本真理的證據就在我們的星球上等待我們獲取 。	as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is just waiting for us on our planet .
我們所在的地方充滿了證據 , 還有物質和能量 。	where we are is filled with evidence , with matter and energy .
而在星系間的空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的前提條件存在的可能性極端之小 。	and in intergalactic space , these three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are incredibly small .
正如我所說 , 那裡空無一物 , 寒冷 , 黑暗 。 抑或不是如此 ?	as i say , there's nothing there , and it's cold and it's dark and it's not ?
事實上 , 這只是另外一個狹隘的誤解 。	in fact , it's just another parochial misconception .
假想在星系間空間有一個立方體存在 , 與我們的房屋般大小 , 太陽系 。 以我們的標準來看 , 這個立方體非常空 , 但是它事實上仍然包含著超過百萬噸的物質 。	imagine a cube in intergalactic space the size of our home , the solar system , by our standards , this cube is very empty , but it's actually remaining more than a million tons of matter .
一百萬噸足夠建造一個 , 比方說 , 自給自足的空間站 , 在這個空間站內聚居著一群科學家 , 他們致力於不斷創造開放式的知識 , 等等 。	a million tons is enough to build , let's say , a selfsufficient space station , a crowd of scientists at this space station , who are dedicated to creating openended knowledge , etc .
然而 , 現在的科技甚至連從星系間空間收集氫氣和將其轉化成別的元素等都遠不能做到 。	however , today's technology is even taking hydrogen from intergalactic space and turning it into other elements and so on .
但問題是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某事是物理定律所允許的 , 那麼在我們知道如何運作的情況下 , 什麼會妨礙我們去實踐它呢 ?	but the question is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it if we know how ?
換句話說 , 這是一個關於知識的問題 , 而不是關於資源 。	in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .
同樣 , 如果我們可以做到的話 , 那麼我們將自動獲得能源供給 , 因為這裡的變化將是核反應堆--證據 ?	and if we can do that , we'll automatically deliver the energy supply , because the change here is the nuclear reactor evidence ?
還是一樣 , 對人類的感官來說那裡漆黑一片 。 但是你所需要做的是拿起一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是今天的技術設計 , 往外看去 , 你會看到我們從這兒看到的同樣的星系 。	again , it's dark out there for human senses , but what you need to do is pick up a telescope , even today's design , and look out and you'll see the same galaxies that we see here .
如果你有一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你將能看到恆星和行星 。	if you have a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars and planets .
在那些星系裡 , 你可以進行天體物理學研究 , 瞭解物理定律 。	in those galaxies , you can do astrophysics and learn the laws of physics .
在你所處的位置 , 你可以製造粒子加速器 , 研究初級粒子物理學 , 化學等 。	where you are , you can build particle accelerators , you can study primary particle physics , chemistry , etc .
也許最難做的科學研究是生物學實地考察 , 因為需要花費數百萬年才能往返最近的有生命的星球 。	perhaps the hardest science to do is biology field trips , because it takes millions of years to get to the nearest lifethreatening planet .
但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , richard--但是我從來都不是那麼喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每數百萬年才進行一次 。	but i have to tell you yes , cheard , i'm sorry , but i never really liked biology field trips , and i think we can do it every millions of years .
因此事實上 , 星系間空間並不具備創造開放式知識的前提條件 。 任何一個這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中任何地方 , 都可以成為跟我們一樣的中心 , 如果履行這一計劃的知識確實存在的話 。	so in fact , intergalactic space doesn't have the prerequisite for the openended creation of knowledge , and any cube like that can be at the same center anywhere in the universe if the knowledge of the project did exist .
因此我們並不是唯一熱情好客的地方 。	so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .
如果星系間空間可以創造出一串開放式的解說 , 那麼幾乎其它所有的環境都是可以的 。 地球也一樣 。 被汙染的地球也是一樣 。	if intergalactic space is capable of creating a series of openended explanations , then pretty much every other environment is ok , and the earth is contaminated , too .
而限制性因素 , 這裡和那裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 而是知識 , 非常匱乏 。	and the limiting factors , here and there , are not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is really scarce .
這樣一個知識型的宇宙觀也許--我認為應該--讓我們感覺非常不平凡 。 但同時也讓我們感覺到自己的脆弱 , 因為這也意味著如果沒有那些必需的具體的知識來幫助我們應對宇宙中源源不斷地挑戰 , 我們將無法生存 。	now , this cosmic knowledgebased view may well , i think we should it feels extraordinary , but it also makes us feel vulnerable , because it also means that without the specific knowledge that we need to help us respond to the universe constantly , we cannot survive .
僅僅是幾光年外的一個超新星爆炸 , 我們都將必死無疑 。	just a few lightyears away from a supernova explosion , we're all going to die undeniably .
martinrees最近剛寫了一本關於我們人類對於所有事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗事故 , 還有最重要的擁有大規模殺傷性武器的恐怖主義 。	martin rees recently wrote a book about our vulnerability with all things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments , and most importantly , terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .
他認為人類文明只有50%的機率可以存活過這個世紀 。	he believed that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .
我想他晚些時候會在這個會上給大家講述 。	and i think he's going to tell you a little bit later at this conference .
但是我認為這一問題並不適合用機率來描述 。	but i don't think that's a good question to describe in odds .
但是我同意他就此的看法 。 我們可以生存下去 , 我們也可能不會存續 。	but i agree with him that we can survive and we may not survive either .
但是這並不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否可以及時創造出相關的知識 。	but it doesn't depend on chance , it's whether we can create the knowledge in time .
這種危險肯定不是前所未有的 。 物種一直都在滅絕 。	the danger is certainly not unprecedented . species have been extinct .
文明也會終止 。 絕大多數存在過的物種和文明都以成歷史 。	civilizations end , and the vast majority of species and civilization have been historical .

上世紀70年代的時候也許就已經太晚了 , 那時候最先進的科學理論告訴我們工業排放將促成一個新的冰河世紀 , 數十億的人類將從此滅亡 。	it's probably already too late in the 1970s , when the most advanced scientific theory tells us that industrial emissions are going to precipitate a new ice age , billions of humans are going to die .

工作很艱難 , 我們乘著一艘帆船某種程度上我們想透過它激起年輕人投身科學的興趣	it's tough . we're riding a sailing boat , and in a way , we want to be interested in piloting the science of young people .
實驗其實非常簡單	the experiments are actually very simple .
採集海水 , 過濾用不同的過濾器採集不同大小的生物然後把它們的dna帶回羅克韋爾的實驗室在那裡我們可以每24小時測完一億字元的遺傳編碼	take the seawater , filter it into different size filters , gather their dna back into the laboratory in rokville , where we can complete 100 million letters of genetic code every 24 hours .
透過這些我們已經有了一些驚人的發現	and through that , we've made some remarkable discoveries .
比如我們眼睛裡的視色素之前認為自然界中只有一到兩種生物擁有和我們一樣的視色素	for instance , even before our eyes were thought that only one or two species in nature have one or two visual pigments like ours .
但後來發現在溫暖海區的上層海水中幾乎每個物種都擁有這類光受體並利用陽光作為能量來源和交流工具	but it turns out that in the upper waters of warm seas , almost every species has this type of light receptor , and uses sunlight as a source and communication tool .
僅僅一個採集點 , 從一桶水中我們就能發現1300萬個新基因相當於5萬個新種	and if you just take a bucket of water and you'll find 13 million new genes , which is equivalent to 50 , 000 new ones .
藉助來自斯隆基金會的資助我們已經將研究擴充套件到空氣中	with funding from the sloan foundation , we've been directing studies into the air .
我們正在測算 , 在我們每天呼吸的空氣中漂浮著多少病毒和細菌特別是在飛機和禮堂等封閉環境中	we're calculating how many viruses and bacteria floating in the air we breathe every day , especially in closed environments like airplanes and auditorium .
我們透過一些簡單的儀器進行過濾在紐約市某棟建築的頂上僅用一天我們就過濾出數十億計的微生物	we've been filtering out some very simple instruments on the roof of a building in new york city , and just a day , we've been filtering out billions of microbes .
目前我們正在對它們進行測序	now we're sequenced .
單純從資料蒐集方面僅僅在加拉帕戈斯群島我們就發現幾乎每200英里我們都能從採集的樣品中看到巨大的多樣性	and just looking at the dataset , it was only in the galapagos , and we found that almost every 200 miles , we can see tremendous diversity in the samples that we harvest .
不同的溫度梯度或許可以部分解釋這種多樣性	this diversity of the temperature gradient can be explained in part .
這是一張基於溫度的衛星圖片紅色表示溫暖區域藍色表示冷的區域我們發現 , 在溫暖海水中獲得樣品與冷海水中的樣品在物種的豐富程度上具有極大的差異	this is an image of a satellite based on temperature , and the red color shows warmth regions , and the cooler regions , and what we find is that samples in warm water have a dramatic difference in the richness of the cold water .
另一個讓我們感到驚奇的事情是這些光受體能探測到不同波長的光而我們能透過它們的氨基酸序列來推測這一過程	another thing that we find surprising is that these photo receptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that through their amino acid sequences .
不同區域之間 , 它們也差別巨大	they're also very different in different areas .
或許不是很讓人驚奇在幾乎是幽藍的深海里光受體傾向於 " 看 " 到藍光	maybe not surprisingly , in the deep , bluegreen receptor tendency , " to see " to blue .
而當週圍存在大量葉綠素的時候它們則 " 看 " 到許多綠光	and when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they're " all green . "
在向較極端的紅外和紫外波段移動時光受體的差別可能更大	the difference between the extreme infrared and ultraviolet period , the light receptors may be even larger .
為了對我們採集的所有基因進行評估我們彙總了所有資料包括到目前為止考察所得的所有資料代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料總共約2900萬個基因	in order to assess all of the genes that we've been gathering , including all the data we've collected so far , all the data we've got about half of all the genetic data on the planet , it's about 29 million genes .
我們把這些基因放入基因家族中試圖回答:我們是發現了已知基因家族中的新成員還是發現了新的基因家族 ?	let's put that into a genomic family to try to answer: did we find new genetically known families , new genetic family to find new genomic family ?
結果表明我們找到了大約5萬個主要的基因家族但我們從環境中獲得的每個新樣品都只是對這些新基因家族的線性補充	it turns out we've found about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we've got from the environment is just a linear replenishment for these new genomes .
因此我們正處在發現地球生命及其組成部分和基因基礎的最初階段	so we're in the very early stages of discovering life and its component parts and genetic building blocks .
我們來看下所謂的進化樹我們人類就在右上角 , 和動物們在一起	let's take a look at what's called an evolutionary tree , and we humans are in the upper righthand corner with animals .
在動物界約2900萬個基因中我們的基因組才僅僅擁有24000個基因	it's about 29 million genes in the animal kingdom , and our genome is just 24 , 000 genes .
如果把所有的動物算在一起我們與之分享著不到30000可能在1.2萬或再多數千的不同的基因家族	if you take all the animals together , we share less than 3 , 000 , we can have 120 , 000 different gene families , probably thousands more .
現在我不僅僅將這些基因視為進化的設計元件	now i'm not just viewing these genes as evolutionary design components .
而且我們要從 " 基因中心觀點 " 或許要追溯到理查德•道金斯的理論而非 " 基因組中心觀點 " 來思考它們對這些基因元件的構造方式是不同的	and we're going to trace back to richard dawkins' theory , not the core of the genome , but the way that they're structured in these genetic components is different .
合成dna , 即人工合成dna的能力在過去的十年或二十年裡與dna測序的能力在某種程度上是同步發展的而且都變得越來越快速和廉價	the ability to synthesize dna , artificially synthesize dna , has been in the past decade or two , somehow developing synchronized , and cheaply .
有關合成基因組的想法是在1995年我們對第二個基因組即生殖道支原體測序的時候想到的	the idea of synthetic genomics was that in 1995 , we came up with the second genital sequence of the genitalia .
我們還製作了相當不錯的t恤寫著 , " 我愛惜我的生殖器 "	we also made a pretty good tshirt , and it said , " i love my genitalia . "
這其實只不過是個微小的生物	it's just a tiny , tiny creature .
卻擁有近500個基因	they have almost 500 genes .
嗜血桿菌擁有1800個基因	haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .
我們提出疑問如果某物種需要800個基因 , 另一種需要500個是否能用一套更小的基因組成一個微小的可運作生命系統	we asked the question: if one species takes 800 genes , 500 of them requires 500 of them to use one smaller set of genomes to make a tiny , viable system .
於是我們開始做轉座子的突變發生	so we started making mutations around seats .
轉座子是隨機插入遺傳編碼之中的短的dna片段	transcriptions are short pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .
如果轉座子插入到基因中間 , 就會擾亂基因的功能	if you insert transposons into genes , they disrupt the function of the genes .
因此我們找出所有能夠接受轉座子插入的基因併為這些 " 非必需基因 " 製作了 " 地圖 "	so we looked at all the genes involved in transplant insertions to make these " nonnecessary genes " maps .
但結果我們發現環境對此的影響非常關鍵我們只能根據環境中確實存在的條件來定義必需和非必需基因	but it turns out that environmental impact is critical , and we can define essential and unnecessary genes according to the environmental existing conditions .
我們還試圖做一個更直觀的研究對13個有親緣關係的生物我們試圖比較它們的基因組 , 看它們是否有相同之處	we're also trying to do a more intuitive study of 13 closely related creatures , and we're trying to compare their genomes to see if they have the same benefits .
於是我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 , 我們發現只有173個基因在這所有13種生物中是相同的	so we got these overlapping circles , and we found that only 173 genes are identical in all 13 species .
如果忽略掉一個細胞內寄生物的話這個基因庫還能擴充套件一點當我們審視核心的一組約310個基因時基因庫擴大更多	if we ignore the gene pool , if we ignore the biological inside of a cell , we can expand more when we look at a core set of 310 genes .
因此我們認為可以從最少500個基因擴充套件或縮小取決你怎麼看這個問題到約300到400個基因	so what we think we can do is , from the minimum of 500 genes , we can expand or shrink the code , tell what you're going to look at , something like 300 to 400 genes .
證明這些理論的唯一方法是以這些基因人工構建一個染色體而且我們必須用基於表達框的方式來達到這一目的	the only way to prove these theories is to construct a chromosome based on these genes , and we need to do it based on framework .
我們發現大片段精確合成dna是非常非常困難的	it turns out that large clips of precision are very , very difficult to synthesize dna .
我的同事漢姆•史密斯和克萊德•哈欽森發明了一個讓人振奮的新方法能讓我們在短短兩週時間內合成一個擁有5000個鹼基對的病毒而且在基因序列和生物學特性上都百分百精確	my colleague , hanm smith and clintson , invented a fascinating new method that enables us to synthesize a virus with 5 , 000 base pairs in just two weeks , and 100 percent in gene sequence and biology .
那是個相當讓人興奮的實驗:我們僅僅把合成的dna片段注進細菌中 , 突然之間dna就開始引導病毒顆粒的合成而病毒反過來殺死了細菌	and that's a pretty exciting experiment: we're just injecting just synthetic pieces of dna into bacteria , and all of a sudden , the dna starts to guide the synthetic particles of the viruses , and viruses are killing the bacteria .
這並非第一個合成的病毒一年前已有某種脊髓灰質炎病毒被製造了出來但這卻是唯一達到百分之一活性的病毒耗時三年才合成成功	this isn't the first synthetic virus , and it's been produced a spinal cord inflammatory virus a year ago , but it's the only one to get to one in a living one in three years to succeed .
這是phix-174結構的一個動畫	this is an animation of phi x 174 .
這是軟體為自己構建硬體的活例子也為我們的生物學提供了新想法	it's an example of how software constructed hardware for itself , and it's provided new ideas for our biology .
有人立即開始擔心生物武器的威脅不久前我也在參議院委員會和另一個由美國政府成立旨在評價這一領域的特殊委員會上作證	someone immediately started worrying about the threat of biological weapons , and soon after , i was at the senate board and another committee with the u . s . government , in order to testify the very special committee in the
我認為最重要的是將事實牢記在心而非人們對事情發生的想象	and i think the most important thing to do is to remember facts , not what they think about what's happening .
基本上 , 任何現在已經被測序的病毒其基因組都可以被合成	basically , any virus that's being sequenced now can be synthesized .
人們立馬被埃博拉病毒或天花病毒之類等嚇壞了但從這些生物體中提取的dna並不具有感染力	people were immediately terrified by things like erbola or smallpox virus , but the dna extracted from these organisms was not contagious .
因此即使有人制成了天花病毒基因組其dna本身並不會引發感染	so even though someone made the smallpox virus genome , the dna itself wouldn't cause infection .
安全部門真正需要擔心的是 " 設計者病毒 "	what's really worrying about security departments is the designer virus .
只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯曾經花大力氣致力於生物武器的研製	only two countries , u . s . and the former soviet union , have spent an effort on biological weapons .
如果這些研究真的已經終止那麼在未來人為製造出設計者病毒的機率微乎其微	if these studies really have ended , the probability of having somebody make a designer virus in the future is very low .
我想兩年內製造出單細胞生物是可能的	i think it's possible to create a singlecelled organism in two years .
而真核細胞我們自己擁有的這種細胞也可能在十年內製造出來	and the nucleus , which we have in our own cells , can be manufactured within a decade .
我們可以區分開進入這個人工基因組的不同表達框和不同基因使得我們能構建數十種不同的結構	we can distinguish between the artificial genome and the framework and the various genes that allow us to construct dozens of different structures .
關鍵是 , 如何把所有其他的放進來 ?	and the key is , how do you put all the rest in ?
我們從這些片段開始然後透過一個同源重組系統將其組合到染色體中	we started with these fragments , and then we combined it in a homologous recombination system .
這來自一種名為耐輻射奇異球菌的生物能在三百萬拉德的輻射劑量下保持活力	this comes from organisms called deinocococcus radiodurans , which remain energized in three million rads of radiation .
在暴露輻射約12到24小時其染色體幾乎完全破碎的情況下它還能將自身的染色體重新組裝起來	in the exposure radiation for 12 to 24 hours , its chromosomes are almost completely broken , and they can reassemble their own chromosomes .
這種生物在地球上幾乎無處不在甚至由於人類的活動它們還可能在外太空活動	this organism is almost everywhere on earth , and even due to human activity , it's possible to be outer spacefaring .
這是玻璃燒杯在約50萬拉德輻射下的情形	this is the context of the glass burning glass , about half a million lads of radiation .
玻璃開始燃燒 , 爆裂而位於底部的微生物則似乎越來越開心	glass starts burning and exploding , and the microbes at the bottom seem to get happier and happier .
這是實際的情形上面是經過170萬拉德輻射之後的染色體	here's the actual scenario with chromosomes 17 million rads of radiation .
幾乎已經支離破碎	it's almost been broken .
下面是24小時之後同樣的dna自動重組的結果	here's what happens 24 hours later with the same dna automatically reconstructed .
這些生物能做到的真是歎為觀止 。 如果不是數以萬計的話也許我們還能找到數以千計的物種也同樣能夠做到	these organisms can really achieve their impressions , and if not for tens of thousands of species , we might be able to find tens of thousands of species as well .
這些基因組合成之後第一步就是將它們移植到另一個沒有基因組的細胞中	once these genomes are synthesized , the first step is to transplant them into cells that have no genome .
因此我們認為合成細胞將具有巨大的前景不僅僅在生物學基礎的理解上而且很可能幫我們應對環境和社會問題	so we think that synthetic cells are going to have a huge promise , not just in biologybased understanding , but it's very likely helping us with environmental and social issues .
例如 , 從我們測序的第三種生物詹氏甲烷球菌 , 生活在相當於水沸點的高溫中以氫作為能量來源並依靠捕獲環境中的二氧化碳為自己提供所需的碳	for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methane bacterium , which is equivalent to the high temperature of the water , hydrogen as an energy source , and depending on carbon dioxide in the environment .
由此可知 , 透過大量不同的途徑數以千計的生物能夠捕獲並依賴二氧化碳生存	so it turns out that through a vast array of different pathways , thousands of animals can capture and depend on co2 .
因此我們可以透過捕獲大氣中的碳製造生物高聚物或其他產品來替代從石油中工業合成的碳製品	so we can do that by capturing biopolymers in the atmosphere , or other products , instead of bioconstructing carbon from oil , industrial carbon .
有種依賴一氧化碳的生物我們利用其還原能力使水分子破裂 , 製造出氫和氧	there are organisms that are dependent on carbon monoxide that we use to crack the water molecules and make hydrogen and oxygen
同樣 , 還有許多途徑能夠用來轉化甲烷	similarly , there are many ways that we can transcribe methane .
杜邦公司和挪威石油公司有一大型專案就是把挪威油氣田中的甲烷轉化為有用的產品	well , dupont and norwegian oil companies have a large project of converting methane from norwegian gasses into useful products .
我突然想到 , 將有一個新的領域 " 組合基因組學 " 很快就要誕生因為有了這些新的合成方法有了這麼龐大的基因序列和同源重組我們可以設計出一個能夠每天生產近百萬個染色體的機器人	and it occurred to me that with a new field of combinatoric genomics , we're going to be born very rapidly , because with these new synthetic methods , with these gigantic sequences and recombinations , we can design a robot that can produce nearly a million chromosomes a day .
因此 , 所有的生物學特徵都能透過螢幕來選擇無論是製造氫化學合成 , 或者僅僅是生存能力	so all of the biological features can be selected by screens , whether it's made of hydrogen chemicals or just survival .
理解這些基因的功能將變得觸手可及	and understanding the function of these genes will become touchable .
我們正嘗試改進光合作用以直接在陽光下製造出氫	we're trying to improve photosynthesis to make hydrogen directly in the sun .
光合作用受氧調節而我們使用的對氧不敏感的氫化酶將完全改變這一過程	photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and the hydrogensensitive enzymes we use are going to completely change the process
我們還整合了多種纖維素酶這些酶可以把複雜的糖類分解為簡單的糖類並在同一個細胞內發酵產生酒精	we also integrated multicellularase enzymes that can break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell .
在一些大型的實驗室裡已經開始利用微生物進行藥品生產	in some very large labs , we've been using microbes to do drugs .
環境中化合物的化學比我們最好的化學家制造出來的化合物還要複雜很多	the chemical compounds in the environment are much more complicated than our best chemists can make compounds .
也許未來的工程物種將成為我們的食物來源能量來源環境補救手段甚至取代石化行業	perhaps future engineering species will be the food source , energy source , environmental rescue , even replacing the fossil industry .
最後讓我以道德和政策上的研究結束吧	let me end with a moral study . let me end with a policy .
我們推遲了1999年開始的實驗直到對是否應該嘗試製造人工物種這一問題進行了一年半的生物倫理學討論後實驗才繼續進行	we late 1999 , and we're late , and we're late , and we're late , and we're late , and we're late , and we're late , and we're late , and we're laying through an artic
每個主要宗教都參與其中	each major religion is involved .
真是一項奇怪的研究因為許多宗教領袖都以他們的教義、經文作為法律而且不能從中找出禁止製造生命的條文所以這應該沒什麼問題最根本的擔憂來自生物武器方面但只有開始進行這些實驗之後我們才能找出從事這一切的原因	and it's a very strange study because many religious leaders are using their creed , their scriptures , and they're not allowed to prohibit the articles of making life , so it's got to be the most fundamental worrying about biological weapons , but it's only after they've started these experiments that we can figure out what's going on .
目前斯隆基金會已經資助了一個相關的多機構參與的研究以確定這些實驗給社會帶來的風險和益處同時也為像我們這樣的科學團隊在這一領域開展研究制定規則在前進的同時我們也努力成為一個良好的榜樣	now , the sloan foundation has funded a multiinstitutional study of participation in making sure that these experiments , the risks and the benefits of the society , but also for the development of research groups like our science team , in the process , we're working to be a good role model .
有許多複雜的議題	there's a lot of complicated issues .
除了生物恐怖主義它們其實都很簡單:我們能否設計出生產清潔能源的工具透過各種不同的簡單步驟或能徹底改變發展中國家的能源生產模式	now , besides bioterrorism , they're simple: can we design tools that produce clean energy , through various simple steps , or they can radically change the means of energy production in the developing world ?
心理學家philipzimbardo說我們大部分人都忽略了幸福和成功的來源:那就是我們觀望過去、面向現在和展望未來 。 要想改善生活質量 , 他建議我們首先要調整時間觀念 。	the psychologist philip zimbardo says that most of us have neglected the source of happiness and success , which is that we look to the past , look to the present and look to the future . to improve the quality of life , he suggested that we first adjust our time perspective .

西蒙•斯涅克用一個簡單但是震撼的模型來闡釋激勵人心的領袖力 , 這個模型的核心是一個 " 黃金 " 圓圈 , 意思是領袖素質的根本來源是回答 " 為什麼 ? " 。 他列舉了蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還有萊特兄弟成功的例子 , 同時以蒂沃數碼錄影機為失敗的典型 。 雖然蒂沃最近打贏一場官司 , 使得其股價上漲了3倍 , 但是它仍在掙扎中 。	simon stenek , in a simple but shocking model , illustrates the elaborate leadership inspiration , which essentially engages in a golden circle , which means the root cause of the leadership is to say , " why ? " he listed the apple , martin luther king and the wright brothers' success story as an example of failing by tide's counting machine , although recently tripling the price of its .
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bull seye , entrepreneur , stream , sales , selling , success .
西蒙•斯涅克:偉大的領袖如何激勵行動	simon stenk: how great leaders can motivate action .
當事情的發展出乎意料之外的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	how can you explain it when things are developing surprisingly ?
換句話說 , 當別人似乎出乎意料地取得成功的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	in other words , how do you explain when people seem to have succeeded unexpectedly ?
比如說 , 為什麼蘋果公司創新能力這麼強 ?	for example , why is apple so innovative ?
這麼多年來 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有競爭對手都更加具有創新性 。	over the years , year after year , they're more innovative than all the competitors .
而其實他們只是一家電腦公司 。	and they're actually just a computer company .
他們跟其他公司沒有任何分別 ,	they're not separate from the other companies .
有同樣的途徑 , 接觸到同樣的人才 , 同樣的代理商 , 顧問 , 和媒體 。	it's the same approach , the exposure to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants and the media .
那為什麼他們就似乎有那麼一點不同尋常呢 ?	so why do they seem a little bit different ?
同樣的 , 為什麼是由馬丁•路德•金來領導民權運動 ?	similarly , why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?
那個時候在美國 , 民權運動之前 , 不僅僅只有他一個人飽受歧視 。 他也決不是那個時代唯一的偉大演說家 。	in the united states at that time , the civil rights movement was not just one person who was discriminated against , but he was not the only great orator of that era .
又為什麼懷特兄弟能夠造出動力控制的載人飛機 , 跟他們相比 , 當時的其他團隊似乎更有能力 , 更有資金 ,	why did the white brothers be able to make motivated manned airplanes that seem to be more capable , more funded than other teams at the time ?
他們卻沒能製造出載人飛機 , 懷特兄弟打敗了他們 。	they hadn't been able to make a description airplane and the white brothers beat them .
一定還有一些什麼別的因素在起作用 。	there must be something else going on .
大概三年半之前 , 我有了個新發現 ,	about three and a half years ago , i made a discovery .
這個發現完全改變了我對這個世界如何運作的看法 。 甚至從根本上改變了我的工作生活方式 。	this discovery completely changed the way i thought about how the world works , and it fundamentally changed the way that i work .
那就是我發現了一種模式 ,	and that's what i found .
我發現世界上所有偉大的令人振奮的領袖和組織 , 無論是蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還是懷特兄弟 , 他們思考、行動、交流溝通的方式都完全一樣 ,	i found out that all the great incredible leaders and organizations in the world , whether it's apple or martin luther king or the white brothers , they're thinking , doing , communicating in exactly the same way .
但是跟所有其他人的方式完全相反 。	but in contrast to what everyone else does .
我所做的僅僅是把它整理出來 。 這可能是世上最簡單的概念 。	all i've done is to organize it . it's probably the simplest concept in the world .
我稱它為黃金圓環 。	i call it the golden circle .
為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 是什麼 ?	why ? how ? what ? what ?
這小小的模型就解釋了為什麼一些組織和領導者能夠在別人不能的地方激發出靈感和潛力 。	this little model explains why organizations and leaders can elicit inspiration and potential where others can't .
我來儘快地解釋一下這些術語 。	let me explain these terms as quickly as i can .
地球上的每個人 , 每個組織都明白自己做的是什麼 , 百分之百 。	everyone on earth knows what they do , 100 percent .
其中一些知道該怎麼做 , 你可以稱之為是你的差異價值 , 或是你的獨特工藝 , 或是你的獨特賣點也好 , 怎麼說都行 。	some of them know what to do , you can call it your differences , or your unique craftsmanship , or your unique selling points , or whatever it is .
但是非常 , 非常少的人和組織明白為什麼做 。	but very , very few people and organizations understand why .
這裡的 " 為什麼 " 和 " 為利潤 " 沒有關係 ,	it's okay with " why " and " profit . "
利潤只是一個結果 , 永遠只能是一個結果 。	profit is just one outcome , it will always be one outcome .
我說的 " 為什麼 " 指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?	and by " why , " i mean , what's your purpose ?
你這樣做的原因是什麼 ? 你懷著什麼樣的信念 ?	what's the reason why you do that ? what are you holding in your beliefs ?
你的機構為什麼而存在 ?	why is your entity there ?
你每天早上是為什麼而起床 ?	why did you get up every morning ?
為什麼別人要在乎你 ?	why should anyone care about you ?
結果是 , 我們思考的方式 , 行動的方式 , 交流的方式都是由外向內的 。	as a result , the way we think , the way we do it , the way we communicate is extroverted .
很顯然的 , 我們所採用的方式是從清晰開始 , 然後到模糊的東西 。	clearly , the way we start is with clarity and blur stuff .
但是激勵型領袖以及組織機構 , 無論他們的規模大小 , 所在領域 , 他們思考 , 行動和交流的方式都是從裡向外的 。	but the incentive leaders and organizations , and no matter their size , they think , move and communicate from the outside .
舉個例子吧 。	let's take an example .
我舉蘋果公司是因為這個例子簡單易懂 , 每個人都能理解 。	i showed apple because it's a simple example , and everybody understands it .
如果蘋果公司跟其他公司一樣 , 他們的市場營銷資訊就會是這個樣子: " 我們做最棒的電腦 ,	if apple were like any other company , their marketing information would be like this: " we make the best computers .
設計精美 , 使用簡單 , 介面友好 。	design beauty , use simple , interface friendly .
你想買一臺嗎 ? " 不怎麼樣吧 。	would you like to buy one ? " not so much .
這就是我們大多數人的交流方式 ,	that's how most of us communicate .
也是大多數市場推廣的方式 , 大部分銷售所採用的方式 , 也是我們大部分人互相交流的方式 。	it's also the way that most markets do what we sell , most of the ways most of us communicate .
我們說我們的職業是幹什麼的 , 我們說我們是如何的與眾不同 , 或者我們怎麼比其他人更好 , 然後我們就期待著一些別人的反應 , 比如購買 , 比如投票 , 諸如此類 。	we say what our profession is doing , we say what we're doing differently , or how we're better than other people , and then we expect other people's reactions , like buying , like voting , and so on .
這是我們新開的的律師事務所 , 我們擁有最棒的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是能滿足客戶的要求 。	it's our new law firm , we have the best lawyer and biggest customers , and we can always satisfy our clients' demands .
這是我們的新車型 , 非常省油 , 真皮座椅 。 買一輛吧 。	this is our new carshaped , very efficient , leather chair . buy a car .
這是蘋果公司實際上的溝通方式:	this is how apple actually communicates .
" 我們做的每一件事情 , 都是為了突破和創新 。	" every single thing we do is to break through and innovate .
我們堅信應該以不同的方式思考 。	we believe that we should think differently .
我們挑戰現狀的方式是透過把我們的產品設計得十分精美 , 使用簡單 , 和介面友好 。	the way we challenge the status quo is by designing our products to be quite exquisite , using simplicity and interface friendships .
我們只是在這個過程中做出了最棒的電腦 。	we're just making the best computer in the process .
想買一臺嗎 ? "	want to buy one ? "
感覺完全不一樣 , 對吧 ? 你已經準備從我這裡買一臺了 。	it feels totally different , right ? you're going to buy one of these from me .
我所做的只是將傳遞資訊的順序顛倒一下而已 。	and what i've done is i've reversed the sequence of the transmission .
事實已經向我們證明 , 人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念和宗旨 。	it turns out that people are buying products that you're not making , people are buying your beliefs and your goals .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people buy products that you're not making , people buy your beliefs .
這就解釋了為什麼這裡的每個人從蘋果公司買電腦時都覺得理所當然 。	which explains why everyone here takes for granted when they buy a computer from apple .
但是我們從蘋果公司買mp3播放器 , 手機 , 或者數碼攝像機時 , 也感覺很舒服 。	but we got mp3 players from apple , mobile phones , digital cameras , and it was also very comfortable .
而其實 , 我剛才已經說過 , 蘋果公司只是個電腦公司 。	and in fact , as i've already said , apple's just a computer company .
沒有什麼能從結構上將蘋果公司同競爭對手區分開來 。	there's nothing that separates apple from structured competitors .
競爭對手和蘋果公司有同樣的能力製造所有這些產品 。	competitors and apple have the same capacity to produce all of these products .
實際上 , 他們也嘗試過 。	actually , they've tried it as well .
幾年前 , 捷威公司推出了平板電視 。	a few years ago , czech released a flatscreen tv .
他們製造平板電視的能力很強 ,	they're very capable of making flatbed tvs .
因為他們做平板顯示器已經很多年了 。	they've been working on tablets for years .
戴爾公司推出了mp3播放器和掌上電腦 , 他們產品的質量非常好 , 產品的設計也非常不錯 。 但是也沒有人買他們的這些產品 。	the d'ore introduced mp3 players and computers , and the mass of their products was great , and the design of the product was good , but nobody bought them .
其實 , 說到這裡 , 我們無法想象會從戴爾公司買mp3播放器 。	in fact , speaking of this , we can't imagine buying an mp3 player from d . c .
你為什麼會從一家電腦公司買mp3播放器呢 ?	why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?
但是每天我們都這麼做 。	but we do it every day .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people buy products that you're not making , people buy your beliefs .
做公司的目標不是要跟所有需要你的產品的人做生意 ,	the company's goal isn't to do business with everybody who needs your product .
而是跟與你有著相同理念的人做生意 。	it's about business with people you have empathy .
這是最精彩的部分 。 我說的這些沒有一個是我自己的觀點 。	it's the most amazing part . none of these are my own perspectives .
這些觀點都能從生物學裡面找到根源 。	all of these ideas can be found in biology .
不是心理學 , 是生物學 。	it's not psychology , it's biology .
當你俯視看大腦的橫截面 , 你會發現人類大腦實際上分成三個主要部分 , 而這三個主要部分和黃金圓環匹配得非常好 。	when you look at the screenshots of the brain , you'll see that the human brain actually is divided into three main components , and those three main components are perfectly matched with the golden
我們最新的腦部 , 管轄智力的腦部 , 或者說我們的大腦皮層 , 對應著 " 是什麼 " 這個圓環 。	our most recent brains , the jurisdictional brain , or our cerebral cortex , correspond to what that is .
大腦皮層負責我們所有的理性和邏輯的思考和語言功能 。	the cortex is responsible for all of our rational and logical thinking and language .
中間的兩個部分是我們的兩個邊腦 。 邊腦負責我們所有的情感 , 比如信任和忠誠 ,	the two portions in the middle are our two brains , and the brain is responsible for all of our emotions , such as trust and loyalty .
也負責所有的行為和決策 , 但這部分沒有語言功能 。	it's in charge of all the behaviors and decisions , but it doesn't have the language .
換句話說 , 當我們由外向內交流時 , 沒錯 , 人們可以理解大量的複雜資訊 , 比如特徵 , 優點 , 事實和圖表 。	in other words , when we're communicating inwardly , yes , people can understand enormous amounts of complex information , features , facts and graphs .
但不足以激發行動 。	but not enough to activate .
當我們由內向外交流時 , 我們是在直接同控制行為的那一部分大腦對話 , 然後我們由人們理性地思考我們所說和做的事情 。	when we're communicating from introverts , we're talking directly to a part of the brain that controls behavior , and we're thinking about what we're saying and what we're doing .
這就是那些發自內心的決定的來源 。	it's the source of those decisions that came from the heart .
你知道 , 有時候你展示給一些人所有的資料圖表 , 他們會說 " 我知道這些資料和圖表是什麼意思 , 但就是感覺不對 。 "	you know , sometimes you show people all the data tables , and they say , " i know what that means , but it just doesn't feel right . "
為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , " 感覺 " 不對 ?	why do we use the verb , the feeling , that we don't ?
因為控制決策的那一部分大腦並不支配語言 ,	because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't govern language .
我們只好說 " 我不知道為什麼 , 就是感覺不對 。 "	we're just like , " i don't know why , it just doesn't feel right . "
或者有些時候 , 你說聽從心的召喚 , 或者說聽從靈魂 。	or sometimes you listen to the calling from the heart , or you listen to the soul .
我不想把這些觀念分解得太徹底 , 但心和靈魂都不是控制行為的部分 。	i don't want to break these ideas down too thoroughly , but hearts and souls are not the part of control .
所有這一切都發生在你的邊腦 , 控制決策行為而非語言的邊腦 。	all of this happens in your brain , controlling decisionmaking , not language .
如果你自己都不知道你為什麼幹你所做的事情 , 而別人要對你的動機作出反應 , 那麼你怎麼可能贏得大家對你的支援 , 從你這裡購買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的 , 對你忠誠並且想成為你正在做的事情的一分子呢 ?	if you don't know why you do what you do and you respond to what you're motivated for , then how can you possibly earn a support from you buying from you , or , more importantly , loyalty to you and want to be a part of what you're doing ?
再說一次 , 目標不僅僅是將你有的東西賣給需要它們的人 ; 而是將東西賣給跟你有共同信念的人 。	and once again , the goal is not just to sell what you have to do to people who need them ; it's to sell to people who share beliefs with you .
目標不僅僅是僱傭那些需要一份工作的人 ; 目標是僱傭那些同你有共同信念的人 。	the goal is not just to employ those who need a job ; the goal is to employ those who share a belief .
你知道嗎 , 我總是說 , 如果你僱傭某人只是因為他能做這份工作 , 他們就只是為你開的工資而工作 , 但是如果你僱傭跟你有共同信念的人 , 他們會為你付出熱血 , 汗水和淚水 。	you know , i always say that if you hire someone who just works on what they're able to do for you , they just work for you , but if you hire servants and you share convictions , they will pay you blood , sweat and tears for you .
這一點 , 沒有比懷特兄弟的故事更恰當的例子了 。	now , there's no more appropriate example of the story of the white brother .
大多數人都沒聽說過塞繆爾•蘭利這個人 。	most of us haven't heard of ermie langley .
20世紀初期 , 投入機動飛行器的熱情就像當今的網站熱 ,	in the early 20th century , the passion for dedicated robots was like the hot website of the day .
每個人都在做嘗試 。	everyone's trying it .
塞繆爾•蘭利擁有所有大家認為是成功的要素 。	samuel ranley has everything that people consider to be successful .
我的意思是 , 即便是現在 , 你問別人 " 為什麼你的產品或者公司失敗了呢 ? "	i mean , even now , you ask people , " why has your product or your company failed ? "
人們總是用同樣的三個東西以同樣的排列順序來回答你 , 缺乏資金 , 用人不善 , 形勢不好 。	people are always using the same three things in the same order , and the lack of money , the terrible people , the bad shape .
總是那三種理由 , 所以讓我們來逐個分析一下 。	there's always those three reasons , so let's go analyzing them .
國防部給了塞繆爾•蘭利5萬美金作為研製飛行器的資金 。	the department of defense funded samuel langley's 50 , 000 dollars as a fund to develop aircraft .
所以說 , 資金不是問題 。	so money isn't a problem .
他在哈佛大學工作過 , 也在史密森尼學會工作過 , 人脈極其廣泛 。 他認識當時最優秀的人才 。	he'd worked at harvard university , he'd worked at the smithsonian , he'd known the best people at the time .
因此 , 他僱傭了用資金能吸引到的最優秀的人才 。 當時的市場形勢相當有利 。	so he's hiring the very best people he can attract , and that's a fairly good market shape .
紐約時報對他做跟蹤報道 , 每個人都支援他 。	the new york times did the report on him , and everyone supported him .
但是為什麼你們連聽都沒聽說過他呢 ?	but why have you never heard of him before ?
與此同時 , 幾百公里之外的俄亥俄州代頓市有一對兄弟 , 奧維爾•萊特和維爾伯•萊特 , 他們倆沒有任何我們認為的成功的要素 。	meanwhile , hundreds of kilometers away in bed newton , ohio , there's a brother , orville and wilbur wright , and they don't have any components of what we think of as success .
他們沒有錢 。 他們用腳踏車店的收入來追求他們的夢想 。 萊特兄弟的團隊中沒有一個人上過大學 , 就連奧維爾和維爾伯也沒有 。 紐約時報更是不沾邊的 。	they had no money . they were pursuing their dreams with a bicycle shop , and none of the teams of the wright brothers were coming to college , not even aville and the vielbor , not even in the new york times especially not nearly as much as the new york times .
不同的是 , 奧維爾和維爾伯追求的是一個事業 , 一個目標 , 一種信念 。	unlike , orville and villeber are pursuing a career , a cause , a belief .
他們相信如果他們能研製出飛行器 , 將會改變全世界的發展程序 。	they believed that if they could build vehicles , it would change the course of the world .
塞繆爾•蘭利就不同了 ,	samuel ranley is different .
他想要發財 , 他想要成名 。	he wanted to be financed . he wanted to be famous .
他追求的是最終結果 ,	what he was looking for was the ultimate result .
是變得富有 。	it's becoming rich .
看吧 , 看接下來怎麼樣了 。	see what happens next .
那些懷有和懷特兄弟一樣夢想的人跟他們一起熱血朝天地奮鬥著 。	those of us with the white brothers who dreamed like them were struggling with their blood .
另一邊的人則是為了工資而工作 。	the other side works for pay .
後來流傳的故事說 , 每次懷特兄弟出去實驗時 , 都必須帶著五組零件 , 因為那是在他們回來吃晚飯之前將要墜毀的次數 。	and it was later the story that every time the white brothers went out , they had to carry all those five components , because that's the number of times they would crash before they return to dinner .
最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 懷特兄弟成功起飛 , 但是當時沒有任何其他人在場目睹 。	and finally , on december 17th , 1903 , the white brothers took off , but nobody else was there .
我們是在幾天後才知道的 。	we didn't know it until a few days later .
後來的事情進一步證實了蘭利動機不純 , 他在懷特兄弟成功的當天就辭職了 。	it further confirmed the langley motivation that he had resigned on the day that the white brothers were successful .
他本來應該可以說: " 夥計們 , 這真是一項偉大的發明 , 我可以改進你們的技術 。 " 但是他沒有 ,	he was supposed to be able to say , " guys , that's a great invention , i can improve your technology , " but he didn't .
因為他不是第一個製造出飛機的人 , 他就不會變得富有 , 他也不會變得有名 , 所以他辭職了 。	because he wasn't the first person to make a plane , he wouldn't become rich , he wouldn't become famous , so he quit .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 而是你的信念 。	people buy not your product ; they buy your beliefs .
如果你講述你的信念 , 你將吸引那些跟你擁有同樣信念的人 。	if you speak about your beliefs , you will attract people who share your beliefs .
但是為什麼吸引那些跟你擁有同樣信念的人非常重要呢 ?	but why is it so important to attract people who share your beliefs ?
創新的傳播有一個規律 , 如果你不知道這個規律 , 你一定了解這個概念 。	innovation has a regular communication , and if you don't know it , you've got to understand it .
我們的社會中 , 有2.5%的人是革新者 。	two and a half percent of our society is a revolutionary .
13.5%的人是早期的少部分採納者 。	thirteen and a half percent were some of the adopters in the early days .
接下來的34%是早期接受的大多數 , 然後是比較晚接受的大多數和最後行動的 。	the next 34% will be the majority of early acceptance , and then the vast majority and final action later .
這部分最後行動的人買按鍵電話的唯一原因是因為他們再也買不到轉盤電話了 。	and the reason for that is that the person that eventually acted to buy the phone was that they couldn't get a phone call anymore .
雖然我們在不同的時候會處在這個曲線上不同的位置 , 但是創新的傳播規律告訴我們如果你想在大眾市場上獲得成功 , 或者要大眾接納一個點子 , 你得等到獲得15%-18%的市場接受度這個轉折點之後才行 。 那時之後市場才真正開啟 。	and although we're at various places on this curve at different times , the rules of innovation tell us that if you're going to succeed in the public market or you're going to take an idea for the public that gets 15 to 18 percent of the market acceptance point , then the markets will be open .
我喜歡問公司: " 你的新生意怎麼樣呀 ? "	i like to ask companies , " what about your new business ? "
他們會很自豪地告訴你 " 哦 , 大概有10%吧 。 "	they'd be proud to tell you , " oh , about 10 percent . "
是呀 , 你有可能就在10%的顧客群這裡過不去了 。	yeah , you're probably going to be here in 10 percent of the customers .
我們都能讓10%的人 " 意會 " ,	we can all get 10 percent of the population to mean " yes . "
對 , 我們一般這樣形容他們 。	yeah , we tend to describe them that way .
就好比描述那種感覺: " 哦 , 他們有點心領神會了 " 。	it's like describing that feeling: " oh , they're a little bit guided by god . "
問題是:你怎麼在他們還沒有成為你的顧客之前就發現那些能意會的人 , 和那些不能意會的人 ?	the question is: how do you find people who , before they've become your customers , people who accidentally didn't ?
這就是問題的所在 , 就是這點間隙 , 你得把這個間隙給填上 , 正如傑弗裡穆爾所說的 , " 跨越鴻溝 " 。 因為早期的大多數不會嘗試新事物 , 除非有些人已經先嚐試過了 。	so that's the problem , and that's the gap , and you need to fill this gap , as jeffrey mull calls it , that the leapfrogging divide is not trying new things in the early days , unless some of you have tried it first .
而這些人 , 創新者和早期的少數人 , 他們喜歡大膽的嘗試 。	and these guys , the innovators and the minorities of the early days , they love the bold experiments .
他們更自然地憑直覺做事情 , 發自於他們的世界觀的直覺 , 而不僅僅是因為市場上有什麼樣的產品 。	they do things more naturally , instinctively , in their view of the world , not just because of the kind of products that are out there in the market .
這是一批在iphone上市的頭幾天去排隊等六個小時來購買的人 , 而其實只要等一個星期你就可以隨便走進店裡從貨架上買到 。	it's a batch of people on the iphone for the first few days to queue for six hours , and in fact , you can take a week and then walk into a store and purchase it from a shelf .
這是一批在平板電視剛推出時會花4萬美金買一臺的人 , 儘管當時的技術還不成熟 。	this is a batch of $40 , 000 buyers at the time of the flatscreen tv , even though the techniques of the time weren't quite ready .
補充說一下 , 他們並不是因為技術的先進而買那些產品 , 而是為了他們自己 。	and by the way , they're not buying products because of technological advancement , but because of themselves .
因為他們想成為第一個體驗新產品的人 。	because they want to be the first to experience a new product .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 人們買的是你的信念 。 你的行動只是證明了你的信念 。	people buy not your product ; people buy your beliefs ; your actions just prove your beliefs .
實際上 , 人們會去做能夠體現他們的信念的事情 。	in fact , people will do things that embody their beliefs .

我們先著眼於大腦海馬區 , 即黃色的區域這是我們的記憶器官 。	we're going to focus on the hippocampus , which is the yellow area , and that's our memory organ .
如果海馬區出現損傷 , 像老年痴呆症患者一樣 , 你將喪失記憶力 , 乃至記不起將車停在了何處 。	if you had damage to the hippocampus , like those with alzheimer's , you would lose your memory , and you wouldn't remember where to park a car .
hippocampus這個詞源自拉丁語 , 有 " 海馬 " 之意因為腦中海馬區的形狀看上去有點像 " 海馬 " 。	hippocampus comes from the latin word " hippocampus , " which means " hippocampus " because the shape of the hippocampus looks a little bit like " seahorse . "
海馬區和大腦其它區域的組成相似 , 都由神經元構成 。	the hippocampus , similar to the rest of the brain , are all made of neurons .
人的大腦由大約一千億個神經元細胞組成 。	our brain consists of about 100 billion neurons .
每個神經元細胞之間透過一些連線中介互相傳送小的電脈衝或者尖峰電壓來進行 " 交流 " 。	each neuron cell sends a small electrical pulse in some connections , or multiple communications in " communication . "
海馬區由兩層片狀的細胞群構成 , 這兩層細胞群緊密相連 。	the hippocampus is made of two patches of cells , and these two layers are tightly linked .
科學家們透過記錄老鼠在某環境中搜羅食物時其腦中單個神經元細胞的反應來了解 " 空間記憶 " 的工作原理與工作機制 。	scientists understand the working principles and work mechanisms of individual neurons in response to a spatial memory response by keeping track of a single neuron in its head .
現在想象一下 , 我們正在為這隻老鼠的海馬區中的一個神經元細胞 " 錄影 " 。	now , imagine for a second that we're recording a neuron in the hippocampus of this mouse .
每當這個細胞發出小型尖峰電壓 , 隨後會出現一個紅點以及咔噠的一聲 。	every time the cell sends out a tiny peak pressure , a red dot and a click .
我們可以看出每當老鼠進入環境中某一特定位置 , 這個神經元細胞便會有反應 。	we can see that the neurons will respond whenever the rat enters a particular location in the environment .
然後這個細胞再透過小型尖峰電壓將以上資訊傳遞給大腦的其它區域 。	and this cell , again , is passing all this information to other parts of the brain via tiny peak peak voltage .
這麼一來 , 我們可以憑藉這個細胞傳送訊號的頻率推知老鼠經過的相應位置 。	so in this way , we can tell from the frequency of the signals that the rat has been touching in front of it .
倘若我們記錄的是很多不同的神經元細胞 , 就會發現當老鼠處於不同的位置上時 , 不同的神經元細胞會產生各自的電訊號 , 正如我們在這些方形中看到的那樣 。	if we were to record many , many different neurons , we'd find that when rats are in different positions , different neurons will produce their own electrical signals , as we see in these squares .
這些訊號為大腦中的其它區域勾勒出一張地圖 , 持續地向大腦指示出 , " 我現在位於環境中的哪個具體點上 ? "	these signals make a map for other brain areas , constantly indicating to the brain , " which specific point am i in right now ? "
我們也記錄人腦中的 " 定位神經元細胞 " 。	we also record the neurons in the human brain .
癲癇病患者有時需要監測他們的腦電活動情況 。	patients with epilepsy sometimes have to monitor their brain activity .
一些患者玩一種電子遊戲 , 遊戲中他們在一個小鎮上自由開車 。	some patients play a video game , and they're driving in a small town .
然後當他們驅車駛過鎮上的某一處時 , 他們大腦海馬區中的 " 定位神經元細胞 " 便會被啟用 , 發出訊號 。	and then when they drive across town somewhere , the neurons in the hippocampus will be activated , sending signals .
那麼這 " 定位細胞 " 是怎麼知道老鼠或人處於某個位置的呢 ?	so how does that region cell know where a mouse or a person is at some point ?
這裡有兩個神經元細胞 , 它們告訴我們 , 在定位時環境的邊界是至關重要的 。	so these are two neurons that tell us that the boundaries of the positioning environment are really important .
上面的這個細胞傾向於在老鼠向盒子中部走去時產生訊號 。	the cell tends to generate signals as the rat moves in the middle of the box .
因此當你將盒子擴大 , 相應的訊號活躍區也隨之擴大 。	so when you expand the box , the response zone gets bigger .
下面的這個喜歡在老鼠緊鄰南面屏障時作出反應 。	this one's favorite to respond when the mouse is tight in the south barrier .
因此當你在盒中放入另一屏障時 , 不論老鼠在盒中何處 , 只要它的南面有屏障 , 該細胞中的相應位置便會同時產生訊號 。	so when you put another barrier in the box , wherever the rats are in the box , if it's got a barrier in the south , it gets a signal in the corresponding position of the cell .
這表明瞭解到達邊界比如周邊的建築物等需要的距離和方向對於海馬區的 " 工作 " 而言至關重要 。	this suggests that understanding the distance and direction of work in the hippocampus is essential .
而且確實 , 在老鼠蒐羅環境時 , 我們在海馬區的輸入訊號中 , 檢測到能對距環境邊界的特定距離與方向作出精確感應的神經元細胞 。	and indeed , in the case of rat gathering the input signals in the hippocampus , we detected specific distances and directions of neurons that accurately sensitive to the environment .
這裡左邊的細胞 , 你可以看出 , 當老鼠向東靠近邊界或屏障時 , 該細胞都會作出反應 , 不論這邊界是一個方盒的邊還是一個圓柱盒的邊甚至是老鼠繞著轉的桌布的垂簾 。	the cell on the left , you can see that when the rat moves towards the east of the border or the barrier , the cell will respond , whether it's a box or a cylinder box or even a curtain around the table of the rat .
而右面的細胞則是在老鼠南面出現邊界時響應 , 不論這邊界是桌布的垂簾還是一堵牆甚至是兩個被隔開的桌子之間的間隙 。	and on the right , the cell responds when it appears in southern mouse borders , whether it's the tableclossed curtain or the gap between two separated tables .
以上是我們所推測的一種 " 定位細胞 " 給動物定位的方式 。	so that's what we're supposed to assume about a static cell for animal positioning .
我們也可檢測 , 人類在簡單環境中 , 是怎樣給諸如這面旗這樣的物體定位的或者乾脆把這物體想成你的車 。	we can also test how humans , in simple environment , are giving objects like this or think about this object as your car .

接著 , 再讓他們回到那個環境 , 通常他們都能根據記憶準確無誤地標出物體所在的位置 。	then , let's get them back to that environment , where usually the objects are , accurately , accurately , accurately , accurately , of the memory .
但在一些試驗中 , 我們會改變環境的形狀和尺度 , 正如我們在 " 定位細胞 " 實驗中所做的那樣 。	but in some trials , we're going to change the shape and scale of the environment just like we did in the experiment with statistical cells .
如此 , 我們可以透過研究實驗者改變環境的形狀和尺度 , 來了解旗幟發生了怎樣的位移	that way , we can learn the shape and scale of the environment by studying experimenters to change the shape and scale of the flag .
比如現在你所看到的 , 假設這面旗幟在如圖中小四方形內的 " × " 的位置 , 然後接著你問人們小旗在哪 , 但實際上你已經將總環境的尺度擴大了 , 結果他們所認為的旗所在的位置也相應地向外擴張 , 而這擴張的模式和 " 定位細胞 " 的一模一樣 。	so for instance , if you look at the flag , say , where the flag is in these little squares , and then you ask people where the flag is , but you actually expand the total scale , and it turns out that what they think the flag is expanding out , and this expansion of patterns and locations is exactly the same as the location of the flag .
這就好像你是透過儲存被某一特定位置所激發的 " 定位細胞 " 產生的訊號模式來記憶小旗的位置的 , 接著當你回到那個地點的時候 , 透過四處打量 , 便可以將你當前腦中 " 定位細胞 " 的訊號模式與之前的模式進行匹配 。	it's as if you were memorizing the positioning patterns of positioning cells through a storage , through a specific location , and then when you get back to that location , you can match what you're used to as the signal patterns of location in your brain that match your patterns with the previous patterns of location .
這個過程便可讓你回到 " 老地方 " 。	and that's where you get to the old place .
我們也能透過位移來給自己定位 。	we can also position ourselves by moving .
因此當我們外出時或許是我們停車後下來隨便走走我們可以給自己定位 , 因為我們可以粗略地將自己的運動路線與大體的返回方向進行整合 。	so when we go out , maybe we park and we walk around we can position ourselves , because we can roughly integrate our motor circuitry with the reversion of the body .
" 定位細胞 " 也能從一種叫做 " 網狀細胞 " 的細胞那兒獲得此類線路整合的資訊 。	region cells also get information from cells called mesh cells , which integrates these circuits .
目前在向海馬區的訊號輸入中又發現了 " 網狀細胞 " , 它們與 " 定位細胞 " 有點類似 。	and so far input to the hippocampus , we've discovered something called mesh cells , and they're sort of like static cells .
隨著老鼠的 " 四處探索 " , 每一個神經元細胞被大量各種位置所激發的訊號組合在一起 , 貫穿整個環境構成一個令人驚歎的規整的三角網格 。	as the mouse " explores around , " each neuron is combined with a signal from so many locations , it stresses throughout the environment to form an extraordinary triangle .
倘若你對一系列 " 網狀細胞 " 進行記錄這裡以不同的顏色區分每一個細胞發出的訊號都能形成網狀 , 遍及整個環境 , 而且每一個細胞的網狀訊號集的位置都與其他細胞有一定偏差 。	so if you document a series of net cells in different colors , each cell can form a web , all the way through to the environment , and every cell's location deviates from other cells .
因此紅色標註的細胞訊號集合在這個網格上 , 綠色的是這個 , 而藍色的是這個 。	so the red cells are put together in this grid , the green one is this , and the blue one is this .
因此綜合來看 , 這就好像老鼠可以在它所到達的環境中建立一個虛擬的位置訊號網這就有點像你在地圖上所看到的經線和緯線 , 只不過要將線替換成 " 三角形 " 。	so in a combination of this , it's as if a rat could build a virtual location signal network in its environment , kind of like the lines and latitudes that you see on the map except for a triangle .

因為所有的網狀訊號集合體都有相同的對稱軸 , 以及相同的網格朝向 , 這裡以橘紅色標識 , 這就意味著大腦中特定部位的所有網狀細胞的聯網行為的變化應該取決於我們是在向著這六個方向運動還是沿著六個方向之間所夾的某一個方向運動 。	because all mesh signals have the same symmetrical axis and the same grid direction , which means that there's an orange red identity , that means that all of the networked behavior of the brain depends on whether we're moving in six directions or in one direction of the six direction .
